Name  :- 
Benoît Berthonneau &lt;ben...@berthonneau.com&gt;  
Subject  :-
RE: Work-around to the Maven restriction on AND condition profile activation?  
Date  :-
Sat, 01 Feb 2014 11:40:47 GMT  
contents:- 
Hi Dave,&#010;&#010;I don't what is the purpose of your double activation profile but I did something that could&#010;help you.&#010;I implement 2 profiles: "should-i-do-something" and "do-something".&#010;&#010; - The "should-i-do-something" profile is automatically activated by the existence of a file&#010;in a project, but the phase of all plugins involved was set to "none" (that's the trick)&#010; - The "do-something" profile is activated on demand and just set the phase(s) of the plugins&#010;involved in the previous profile&#010;&#010;Hope this help,&#010;Benoît.&#010;&#010;&#010;-----Message d'origine-----&#010;De : laredotornado-3 [mailto:laredotornado@gmail.com] &#010;Envoyé : vendredi 31 janvier 2014 22:19&#010;À : users@maven.apache.org&#010;Objet : Work-around to the Maven restriction on AND condition profile activation?&#010;&#010;Hi,&#010;&#010;I’m using Maven 3.1.1 and Java 1.6.  From reading over posts online, it seems a profile&#010;cannot be activated based on two conditions (i.e. there is no such thing as logical AND in&#010;Maven profile activation).  So I was wondering if someone knows of a work-around for what&#010;I want to do.  I want to run a plugin if a flag is given on the command line (“-DdeployWars”)&#010;and a file is present in my module, e.g.&#010;&#010;                        &lt;activation&gt;&#010;                                &lt;file&gt;&#010;&#010;&lt;exists&gt;${basedir}/src/main/webapp/WEB-INF/web.xml&lt;/exists&gt;&#010;                                &lt;/file&gt;&#010;                        &lt;/activation&gt;&#010;&#010;Unfortunately, its not an option to include the AND profile activation extension (https://github.com/johnjcool/and-activation-profile-selector)&#010;in our Maven installation, unless there is some way to reference that extension from the Maven&#010;project itself.&#010;&#010;Thanks for your thoughts, - Dave&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;--&#010;View this message in context: &#010;http://maven.40175.n5.nabble.com/Work-around-to-the-Maven-restriction-on-AND-condition-profile-activation-tp5782919.html&#010;Sent from the Maven - Users mailing list archive at Nabble.com.&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Name  :- 
Russ Tremain &lt;ru...@releasetools.org&gt;  
Subject  :-
enough entropy for jarsigning?  
Date  :-
Sat, 01 Feb 2014 18:38:30 GMT  
contents:- 
Hi,&#010;&#010;I ran into a very weird problem the other day that I thought I would &#010;share with the list.&#010;&#010;We recently switched our maven builds to Fedora linux running on a &#010;really great VMWARE cluster with very fast SSD-based storage.&#010;&#010;However, our average java build inexplicably increased to several &#010;hours.  In my own build environment under mac osx, similar builds &#010;would complete in minutes (some of the small builds take only 2-3 &#010;minutes under normal circumstances).&#010;&#010;I eventually noticed that the jobs were hanging during jarsigning.&#010;&#010;After investigating many red herrings, it boiled down to the linux &#010;"secure random" device, /dev/random, not supplying enough data.  It &#010;is a blocking device, and therefore, if you are using the jarsigner &#010;plugin, the jarsigner will read from /dev/random to seed the &#010;encryption for the signature for each class.  If you have a jar with &#010;many classes that need to be signed, it can literally take hours.&#010;&#010;In our case, a 2 minute build was taking up to 4 hours.&#010;&#010;Note that if you are running under mac osx, this will not occur, &#010;because Apple maps /dev/random to the psuedo random number device &#010;which is /dev/urandom:&#010;&#010;# ls -l /dev/random /dev/urandom&#010;crw-rw-rw-  1 root  wheel    9,   0 Feb  1 09:31 /dev/random&#010;crw-rw-rw-  1 root  wheel    9,   1 Jan 23 19:22 /dev/urandom&#010;&#010;You may not experience this problem if you are running on real &#010;hardware, because the so-called "entropy pool" can be supplied with &#010;hardware sources of noise, even at the chip level in some cases.&#010;&#010;However, if you are running in a virtual environment, apparently &#010;there is not enough noise to supply the entropy pool with a steady &#010;stream of data, and so /dev/random runs out and blocks very quickly.&#010;&#010;The problem is very easy to detect:&#010;&#010;&#009;$ dd if=/dev/random of=/dev/null bs=1 count=1000&#010;&#010;If dd hangs while reading from the device, or takes a very long time, &#010;then you have the problem.&#010;&#010;Once you identify the problem, it is easy to solve [1,2].  In our &#010;case, we opted for a system-wide solution using the rngd-tools [3] &#010;package, since this problem can impact many things, including ssl &#010;connections with jenkins [4], or any other programs that consume &#010;encryption services.&#010;&#010;Cheers,&#010;-Russ&#010;&#010;References:&#010;&#010;[1] &#010;http://stackoverflow.com/questions/137212/how-to-solve-performance-problem-with-java-securerandom&#010;[2] http://docs.oracle.com/cd/E12529_01/wlss31/configwlss/jvmrand.html&#010;[3] on fedora/centos/etc:  sudo yum install rng-utils&#010;     start daemon with:  rngd --rng-device=/dev/urandom&#010;[4] &#010;"&lt;https://groups.google.com/forum/?hl=en_US#!searchin/jenkinsci-users/Re$3A$20How$20does$20Jenkins$20checkout$20sources$20from$20svn$20to$20the$20slaves/jenkinsci-users/sqp6hvzdXDY/P-ZYkDO-8TgJ&gt;How&#010;&#010;does Jenkins checkout sources from svn to the slaves", &#010;jenkinsci-users list.&#010;&#010;

Re: dependency management across projects  
Date  :-
Sun, 02 Feb 2014 08:34:17 GMT  
contents:- 
On Fri, Jan 31, 2014 at 1:16 PM, Anders Hammar &lt;anders@hammar.net&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; The release of the BOM would be that release of "a single coherent unit"&#010;&gt; then. It would specify the (marketing) version of the "platform" P.&#010;&gt; For example, P v1.0.0 will include v1.2.3 of SP1 (sub-product 1), v1.4.3 of&#010;&gt; SP2, etc.&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;Isn't it what I just write in my original post? (without mentioning the BOM)&#010;&#010;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Creating the BOM would be a manual work I think, as you want to make sure&#010;&gt; that exactly the correct versions are included (might not be the latest&#010;&gt; releases).&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;Yes, this is already what I do. The very point I am trying to make here is&#010;"how do you manage that manual BOM on a daily basis". Each sub-project has&#010;its own release cycle and we cannot force the versions it has to use for a&#010;specific branch. For instance, the product might state that the dependency&#010;D should be 2.2.0 (because that's the latest or the one that people&#010;generally use) but for backward compatibility reason SP2 has to use 1.8.0.&#010;&#010;Creating manually the first BOM for P v1.0.0 isn't a problem: i've created&#010;a set of tools that I am happy to share once they are fully ready. But&#010;maintaining that BOM in the long run is more of a challenge (because we&#010;can't force the sub-projects to use those versions so we have to monitor&#010;what happens in each sub-project to take the appropriate version at the&#010;product level).&#010;&#010;Thanks again for the feedback!&#010;&#010;S.&#010;&#010;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; /Anders&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; There is also the possibility of creating a "grouping pom", which lists&#010;&gt; &gt; all&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; artifacts as dependencies. You would then declare a dependency to that&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; grouping pom and get all deps magically sucked in. However, this is not&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; really the "Maven way" in my opinion as you wouldn't specify your&#010;&gt; direct&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; deps bu sort of relly on transitive deps. There are some fans of this&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; approach though here on this list.&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; 2. Build configs that *force* each sub-project to run with the list&#010;&gt; of&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; dependencies for the project (to ensure all tests pass, etc). This is&#010;&gt; &gt; to&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; be&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; used alongside the regular build job for validation purpose&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; Maybe some enforcer rule?&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; Like I said, this is to be used alongside the regular build job. So my&#010;&gt; SP4&#010;&gt; &gt; 1.2.0-SNAPSHOT is building with a set of dependencies on its own and I&#010;&gt; want&#010;&gt; &gt; to validate that with the dependencies of the target release for P, it is&#010;&gt; &gt; also working just fine. It may just be the same ideally or slightly&#010;&gt; &gt; different (or not slightly at all which requires an explicit validation).&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; So I need to be able to swap those versions for validation purposes and&#010;&gt; run&#010;&gt; &gt; the build with that.&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; S.&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; /Anders&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; I started to look at this and my first trial was to generate a report&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; with&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; all the dependencies of each project and build a consolidated report&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; that I&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; can match against the candidates. This would help manage the first&#010;&gt; goal&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; as&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; if a dependency gets added, removed or updated, the global&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; dependencyManagement has to be impacted manually (do we upgrade or&#010;&gt; not,&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; etc).&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; For the second part, it's not easy to force a dependency change in&#010;&gt; &gt; Maven,&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; especially if the version has been specified at the project level.&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; Thanks for reading that far. If you have any idea or know any&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; organisation&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; that tried to implement that, I'd be interested&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; Thanks!&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; S.&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;

&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; The release of the BOM would be that release of "a single coherent unit"&#010;&gt; &gt; then. It would specify the (marketing) version of the "platform" P.&#010;&gt; &gt; For example, P v1.0.0 will include v1.2.3 of SP1 (sub-product 1), v1.4.3&#010;&gt; of&#010;&gt; &gt; SP2, etc.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Isn't it what I just write in my original post? (without mentioning the&#010;&gt; BOM)&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;I believe so, yes. The key thing in my "solution" is the BOM. And the BOM&#010;will keep the appropriate version of the the sub-products together.&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&gt; The very point I am trying to make here is&#010;&gt; "how do you manage that manual BOM on a daily basis". Each sub-project has&#010;&gt; its own release cycle and we cannot force the versions it has to use for a&#010;&gt; specific branch. For instance, the product might state that the dependency&#010;&gt; D should be 2.2.0 (because that's the latest or the one that people&#010;&gt; generally use) but for backward compatibility reason SP2 has to use 1.8.0.&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;There is no automatic solution for this that I know of. I suppose that&#010;tolls could be created, but keep in mind that in the end, "for backward&#010;compatibility reason SP2 has to use 1.8.0" is normally a human decision.&#010;&#010;/Anders&#010;&#010;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Creating manually the first BOM for P v1.0.0 isn't a problem: i've created&#010;&gt; a set of tools that I am happy to share once they are fully ready. But&#010;&gt; maintaining that BOM in the long run is more of a challenge (because we&#010;&gt; can't force the sub-projects to use those versions so we have to monitor&#010;&gt; what happens in each sub-project to take the appropriate version at the&#010;&gt; product level).&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Thanks again for the feedback!&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; S.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; /Anders&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; There is also the possibility of creating a "grouping pom", which&#010;&gt; lists&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; all&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; artifacts as dependencies. You would then declare a dependency to&#010;&gt; that&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; grouping pom and get all deps magically sucked in. However, this is&#010;&gt; not&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; really the "Maven way" in my opinion as you wouldn't specify your&#010;&gt; &gt; direct&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; deps bu sort of relly on transitive deps. There are some fans of this&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; approach though here on this list.&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; 2. Build configs that *force* each sub-project to run with the list&#010;&gt; &gt; of&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; dependencies for the project (to ensure all tests pass, etc). This&#010;&gt; is&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; to&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; be&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; used alongside the regular build job for validation purpose&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; Maybe some enforcer rule?&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; Like I said, this is to be used alongside the regular build job. So my&#010;&gt; &gt; SP4&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; 1.2.0-SNAPSHOT is building with a set of dependencies on its own and I&#010;&gt; &gt; want&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; to validate that with the dependencies of the target release for P, it&#010;&gt; is&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; also working just fine. It may just be the same ideally or slightly&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; different (or not slightly at all which requires an explicit&#010;&gt; validation).&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; So I need to be able to swap those versions for validation purposes and&#010;&gt; &gt; run&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; the build with that.&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; S.&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; /Anders&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; I started to look at this and my first trial was to generate a&#010;&gt; report&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; with&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; all the dependencies of each project and build a consolidated&#010;&gt; report&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; that I&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; can match against the candidates. This would help manage the first&#010;&gt; &gt; goal&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; as&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; if a dependency gets added, removed or updated, the global&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; dependencyManagement has to be impacted manually (do we upgrade or&#010;&gt; &gt; not,&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; etc).&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; For the second part, it's not easy to force a dependency change in&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; Maven,&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; especially if the version has been specified at the project level.&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; Thanks for reading that far. If you have any idea or know any&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; organisation&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; that tried to implement that, I'd be interested&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; Thanks!&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; S.&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;

Hi everyone,&#010;&#010;&gt; &gt; The very point I am trying to make here is&#010;&gt; &gt; "how do you manage that manual BOM on a daily basis".&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; There is no automatic solution for this that I know of.&#010;&#010;Maybe not exactly what you are looking for, but sort of similar:&#010;&#010;My group uses a script [1] to automatically bump the version of our parent&#010;POM [2].&#010;&#010;In that parent POM, we declare many version properties, plugin&#010;configuration in pluginManagement, etc., and we like to keep all our&#010;projects across various Git repositories using the newest available version&#010;of the parent, to minimize version clashes when mixing and matching&#010;libraries.&#010;&#010;We set up a parameterized Jenkins job [3] to run the parent bump for us,&#010;which provides checkboxes for all the downstream projects so the bump can&#010;be controlled individually.&#010;&#010;It's not perfect but it does save a lot of manual maintenance.&#010;&#010;Regards,&#010;Curtis&#010;&#010;[1]&#010;https://github.com/scijava/scijava-scripts/blob/a0fc8006741e0216c74c82866fd1bb1a7d364d55/bump-pom-scijava.sh&#010;[2]&#010;https://github.com/scijava/pom-scijava/blob/0de0676f7731b98baa89379dc8b92f8b26a5d086/pom.xml&#010;[3] http://jenkins.imagej.net/view/SciJava/job/Bump-POM-SciJava/&#010;&#010;&#010;On Mon, Feb 3, 2014 at 1:21 AM, Anders Hammar &lt;anders@hammar.net&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; The release of the BOM would be that release of "a single coherent&#010;&gt; unit"&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; then. It would specify the (marketing) version of the "platform" P.&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; For example, P v1.0.0 will include v1.2.3 of SP1 (sub-product 1),&#010;&gt; v1.4.3&#010;&gt; &gt; of&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; SP2, etc.&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; Isn't it what I just write in my original post? (without mentioning the&#010;&gt; &gt; BOM)&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I believe so, yes. The key thing in my "solution" is the BOM. And the BOM&#010;&gt; will keep the appropriate version of the the sub-products together.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; The very point I am trying to make here is&#010;&gt; &gt; "how do you manage that manual BOM on a daily basis". Each sub-project&#010;&gt; has&#010;&gt; &gt; its own release cycle and we cannot force the versions it has to use for&#010;&gt; a&#010;&gt; &gt; specific branch. For instance, the product might state that the&#010;&gt; dependency&#010;&gt; &gt; D should be 2.2.0 (because that's the latest or the one that people&#010;&gt; &gt; generally use) but for backward compatibility reason SP2 has to use&#010;&gt; 1.8.0.&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; There is no automatic solution for this that I know of. I suppose that&#010;&gt; tolls could be created, but keep in mind that in the end, "for backward&#010;&gt; compatibility reason SP2 has to use 1.8.0" is normally a human decision.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; /Anders&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; Creating manually the first BOM for P v1.0.0 isn't a problem: i've&#010;&gt; created&#010;&gt; &gt; a set of tools that I am happy to share once they are fully ready. But&#010;&gt; &gt; maintaining that BOM in the long run is more of a challenge (because we&#010;&gt; &gt; can't force the sub-projects to use those versions so we have to monitor&#010;&gt; &gt; what happens in each sub-project to take the appropriate version at the&#010;&gt; &gt; product level).&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; Thanks again for the feedback!&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; S.&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; /Anders&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; There is also the possibility of creating a "grouping pom", which&#010;&gt; &gt; lists&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; all&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; artifacts as dependencies. You would then declare a dependency to&#010;&gt; &gt; that&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; grouping pom and get all deps magically sucked in. However, this&#010;is&#010;&gt; &gt; not&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; really the "Maven way" in my opinion as you wouldn't specify your&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; direct&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; deps bu sort of relly on transitive deps. There are some fans of&#010;&gt; this&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; approach though here on this list.&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; 2. Hi Jörg,&#010;&#010;&gt; We use simply "x-SNAPSHOT" for the parent version. That way no&#010;&gt; unreleased project has to be touched, it simply uses the "lastest"&#010;&gt; SNAPSHOT of the parent. No script required.&#010;&#010;Yeah, that is very convenient, if you are willing to accept the two-edged&#010;sword of irreproducible builds. A breaking change in the parent will break&#010;all builds that consume it... but can be fixed just as easily too without&#010;touching the downstream projects.&#010;&#010;Of course, it's a decision every project has to make for themselves. My&#010;projects opted for build reproducibility by using only release linkages&#010;(for parent POMs, dependencies and plugins). This has many advantages:&#010;e.g., "git bisect" fully works as one might hope, allowing you to resurrect&#010;the state of the code even from years prior and still build successfully.&#010;The downside is that you must make releases in order to be able to pin to&#010;them.&#010;&#010;Regards,&#010;Curtis&#010;&#010;&#010;On Tue, Feb 4, 2014 at 4:38 AM, Jörg Schaible&#010;&lt;joerg.schaible@swisspost.com&gt;wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; Curtis Rueden wrote:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; Hi everyone,&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; &gt; The very point I am trying to make here is&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; &gt; "how do you manage that manual BOM on a daily basis".&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; There is no automatic solution for this that I know of.&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; Maybe not exactly what you are looking for, but sort of similar:&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; My group uses a script [1] to automatically bump the version of our&#010;&gt; parent&#010;&gt; &gt; POM [2].&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; We use simply "x-SNAPSHOT" for the parent version. That way no unreleased&#010;&gt; project has to be touched, it simply uses the "lastest" SNAPSHOT of the&#010;&gt; parent. No script required.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; [snip]&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; - Jörg&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; ---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;&gt; To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt; For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;

Hi Curtis,&#010;&#010;Curtis Rueden wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; Hi Jörg,&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt; We use simply "x-SNAPSHOT" for the parent version. That way no&#010;&gt;&gt; unreleased project has to be touched, it simply uses the "lastest"&#010;&gt;&gt; SNAPSHOT of the parent. No script required.&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; Yeah, that is very convenient, if you are willing to accept the two-edged&#010;&gt; sword of irreproducible builds.&#010;&#010;What do you mean with "irreproducible builds"? Definitely, if you project &#010;relies on a SNAPSHOT parent, it does not matter if you call it 1-SNAPSHOT or &#010;x-SNAPSHOT.&#010;&#010;&gt; A breaking change in the parent will break&#010;&gt; all builds that consume it... but can be fixed just as easily too without&#010;&gt; touching the downstream projects.&#010;&#010;Well, somebody obviously made the choice for the SNAPSHOT parent ... with &#010;all consequences.&#010;&#010;&gt; Of course, it's a decision every project has to make for themselves. My&#010;&gt; projects opted for build reproducibility by using only release linkages&#010;&gt; (for parent POMs, dependencies and plugins). This has many advantages:&#010;&gt; e.g., "git bisect" fully works as one might hope, allowing you to&#010;&gt; resurrect the state of the code even from years prior and still build&#010;&gt; successfully. The downside is that you must make releases in order to be&#010;&gt; able to pin to them.&#010;&#010;Once a project is released, you also have a released parent. No surprises &#010;anymore. And the project can then make its own decision if it creates also a &#010;branch for the parent and rely on e.g. 254.x-SNAPSHOT either for maintenance &#010;releases or further development.&#010;&#010;This scheme works well for us now for several years.&#010;&#010;Cheers,&#010;Jörg&#010;&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Name  :- 
Curtis Rueden &lt;ctrue...@wisc.edu&gt;  
Subject  :-
Re: dependency management across projects  
Date  :-
Thu, 06 Feb 2014 20:11:38 GMT  
contents:- 
Hi Jörg,&#010;&#010;&gt; What do you mean with "irreproducible builds"?&#010;&#010;I mean that you may build the same source code today, and then again next&#010;week, and the two build results may differ.&#010;&#010;With our projects we wanted the certainty that if you checked out *any*&#010;revision from the SCM history, you would still be able to build it in, say,&#010;5 years... at least as long as you use the same versions of the tooling&#010;(Java version etc.).&#010;&#010;With a SNAPSHOT parent, that is not guaranteed. You may introduce a change&#010;in the parent that causes a build to fail when it used to succeed, which&#010;makes "bisect" style debugging no longer feasible. That is, if old SCM&#010;revisions no longer build properly due to changes in the parent, you will&#010;no longer be able to perform a binary search through the SCM history to&#010;determine the exact commit which introduced a bug.&#010;&#010;&gt; This scheme works well for us now for several years.&#010;&#010;Sure, and I'm not dissing it, just pointing out the pros and cons. We&#010;wanted fully reproducible builds, which meant that even our SNAPSHOT&#010;revisions have only release dependencies, including the parent POM&#010;reference. This indeed has some negative consequences, such as needing that&#010;script to bump things for us, rather than everything "Just Working" with no&#010;changes. And you're right that *release* version builds are still&#010;reproducible either way.&#010;&#010;Regards,&#010;Curtis&#010;&#010;&#010;On Wed, Feb 5, 2014 at 1:54 AM, Jörg Schaible&#010;&lt;joerg.schaible@swisspost.com&gt;wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; Hi Curtis,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Curtis Rueden wrote:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; Hi Jörg,&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; We use simply "x-SNAPSHOT" for the parent version. That way no&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; unreleased project has to be touched, it simply uses the "lastest"&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt; SNAPSHOT of the parent. No script required.&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; Yeah, that is very convenient, if you are willing to accept the two-edged&#010;&gt; &gt; sword of irreproducible builds.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; What do you mean with "irreproducible builds"? Definitely, if you project&#010;&gt; relies on a SNAPSHOT parent, it does not matter if you call it 1-SNAPSHOT&#010;&gt; or&#010;&gt; x-SNAPSHOT.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; A breaking change in the parent will break&#010;&gt; &gt; all builds that consume it... but can be fixed just as easily too without&#010;&gt; &gt; touching the downstream projects.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Well, somebody obviously made the choice for the SNAPSHOT parent ... with&#010;&gt; all consequences.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; Of course, it's a decision every project has to make for themselves. My&#010;&gt; &gt; projects opted for build reproducibility by using only release linkages&#010;&gt; &gt; (for parent POMs, dependencies and plugins). This has many advantages:&#010;&gt; &gt; e.g., "git bisect" fully works as one might hope, allowing you to&#010;&gt; &gt; resurrect the state of the code even from years prior and still build&#010;&gt; &gt; successfully. The downside is that you must make releases in order to be&#010;&gt; &gt; able to pin to them.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Once a project is released, you also have a released parent. No surprises&#010;&gt; anymore. And the project can then make its own decision if it creates also&#010;&gt; a&#010;&gt; branch for the parent and rely on e.g. 254.x-SNAPSHOT either for&#010;&gt; maintenance&#010;&gt; releases or further development.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; This scheme works well for us now for several years.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Cheers,&#010;&gt; Jörg&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; ---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;&gt; To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt; For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;

You could use Maven Shade plugin with the option minimizeJar and check the resulting Uber-JAR.&#010;&#010;Maybe even better is ProGuard (the shrinker part without the obfuscator). It will even detect&#010;some uses of class.forName if they are not using dynamic strings. By trial and error you can&#010;exclude some essential classes or packages from shrinking and the remaining stuff in your&#010;Uber-JAr again tells you how many and which dependencies your program is actually using.&#010;-- &#010;Alexander Kriegisch&#010;&#010;&#010;&gt; Hervé Boutemy &lt;hbout...@apache.org&gt;  
Subject  :-
[ANN] Apache Maven SCM Publish Plugin 1.0 Released  
Date  :-
Tue, 04 Feb 2014 07:23:45 GMT  
contents:- 
The Apache Maven team is pleased to announce the release of the Apache Maven &#010;SCM Publish Plugin, version 1.0&#010;&#010;The maven-scm-publish-plugin is a utility plugin to allow publishing Maven &#010;website to any supported SCM. The primary goal was to have an utility plugin &#010;to allow Apache projects to publish Maven websites via the ASF svnpubsub &#010;system. The plugin has been tested with git scm too and by example can push &#010;content for github pages.&#010;&#010;http://maven.apache.org/plugins/maven-scm-publish-plugin/&#010;&#010;You should specify the version in your project's plugin configuration:&#010;&#010;&lt;plugin&gt;&#010;  &lt;groupId&gt;org.apache.maven.plugins&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;  &lt;artifactId&gt;maven-scm-publish-plugin&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;  &lt;version&gt;1.0&lt;/version&gt;&#010;&lt;/plugin&gt;&#010;&#010;&#010;Release Notes - maven-scm-publish-plugin - Version 1.0&#010;&#010;** Improvement&#010;    * [MSCMPUB-6] - when creating a directory in svn, if checkout fails, wait &#010;a few seconds and retry&#010;    * [MSCMPUB-7] - Add timestamp when commit starts (and ends)&#010;    * [MSCMPUB-10] - Pick up SCM credentials from settings.xml server section&#010;    * [MSCMPUB-11] - display content size (number of directories, files, and &#010;size)&#010;&#010;** Story&#010;    * [MSCMPUB-4] - Need a working example for GitHub/gh-pages, preferably &#010;naturally linked to natural site lifecycle, and multi-module&#010;&#010;** Task&#010;    * [MSCMPUB-3] - Upgrade to SCM-1.9&#010;&#010;Enjoy,&#010;&#010;-The Apache Maven team&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

current scm-providers cause I can see this problem only increasing as&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; more&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; people a) upgrade git or b) move to git and get pissed off with&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; maven+git&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; This work around works, but really - goes against convention over&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; configuration.&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; On 27 Dec 2013, at 1:43, Robert Scholte wrote:&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; &gt; I don't think this will fix the issue.&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; &gt; SCM 1.8.1[1] is not related to GIT 1.8.x&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; &gt; It's a coincidence that the most recent version of SVN, GIT and SCM&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; are&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; all 1.8.x&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; When I build my Maven project with dependencies (using Netbeans but pointing&#010;to a vanilla Maven installation), I get BUILD SUCCESS. Great!&#010;&#010;When I try to /run /it in the form of *java -cp&#010;target/my-app-1.0-SNAPSHOT.jar com.mycompany.app.App* I get this:&#010;*java.lang.NoClassDefFoundError: org/slf4j/LoggerFactory*&#010;&#010;How come this dependency fails at this late stage?&#010;&#010;Trying to run the class from NetBeans itself gives a different error:&#010;*Failed to execute goal org.codehaus.mojo:exec-maven-plugin:1.2.1:exec*&#010;&#010;Please enlighten me as to how I can run this thing. It works fine in Eclipse&#010;when I run it as a Java Application - but Eclipse has other problems that&#010;I'm avoiding so I need to do this either from CLI or NetBeans (preferable).&#010;&#010;Thanks,&#010;Ten&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;--&#010;View this message in context: http://maven.40175.n5.nabble.com/Build-is-successful-but-can-t-run-tp5783294.html&#010;Sent from the Maven - Users mailing list archive at Nabble.com.&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Name  :- 
Wayne Fay &lt;wayne...@gmail.com&gt;  
Subject  :-
Re: Build is successful but can't run?  
Date  :-
Wed, 05 Feb 2014 18:23:05 GMT  
contents:- 
&gt; When I try to /run /it in the form of *java -cp&#010;&gt; target/my-app-1.0-SNAPSHOT.jar com.mycompany.app.App* I get this:&#010;&gt; *java.lang.NoClassDefFoundError: org/slf4j/LoggerFactory*&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; How come this dependency fails at this late stage?&#010;&#010;This line says "run Java with the classpath being my-app.jar and use&#010;com.mycompany.app.App as the main/entry class."&#010;&#010;Java says OK and happily tries to run your file. Then immediately&#010;discovers that the classpath you have specified does not include one&#010;or more classes - classes that you have declared as dependencies and&#010;by using Maven to help manage during the compile process you don't&#010;need to worry about the details of your classpath. This is exactly&#010;correct.&#010;&#010;But now you are dealing with run-time, not compile-time. Until now,&#010;Maven has ensured that various dependencies are in the classpath --&#010;but note that you are not running Maven, you are running Java, and&#010;java does not know anything about Maven's pom and the dependencies&#010;etc. So now you need to manually build out that classpath to run your&#010;code with a lot more things in the -cp parameter.&#010;&#010;A far simpler approach is to use the maven-exec-plugin and again let&#010;Maven help with your run-time dependencies. Here is a link to that&#010;documentation - I'm sure you can sort it out by click a few links and&#010;doing 5 minutes of reading:&#010;http://mojo.codehaus.org/exec-maven-plugin/&#010;&#010;Wayne&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

On 2/5/2014 9:52 AM, TenLeftFingers wrote:&#010;&gt; When I build my Maven project with dependencies (using Netbeans but pointing&#010;&gt; to a vanilla Maven installation), I get BUILD SUCCESS. Great!&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; When I try to /run /it in the form of *java -cp&#010;&gt; target/my-app-1.0-SNAPSHOT.jar com.mycompany.app.App* I get this:&#010;&gt; *java.lang.NoClassDefFoundError: org/slf4j/LoggerFactory*&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; How come this dependency fails at this late stage?&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Trying to run the class from NetBeans itself gives a different error:&#010;&gt; *Failed to execute goal org.codehaus.mojo:exec-maven-plugin:1.2.1:exec*&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Please enlighten me as to how I can run this thing. It works fine in Eclipse&#010;&gt; when I run it as a Java Application - but Eclipse has other problems that&#010;&gt; I'm avoiding so I need to do this either from CLI or NetBeans (preferable).&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Thanks,&#010;&gt; Ten&#010;&#010;I normally use NetBeans . . . .&#010;&#010;One way to handle this (and it'll end up looking like a standard &#010;NetBeans project) is the following.&#010;&#010;1. Modify the manifest via the maven-jar-plugin&#010;&#010;&lt;plugin&gt;&#010;   &lt;groupId&gt;org.apache.maven.plugins&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;   &lt;artifactId&gt;maven-jar-plugin&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;   &lt;version&gt;2.4&lt;/version&gt;&#010;   &lt;configuration&gt;&#010;     &lt;archive&gt;&#010;       &lt;manifest&#010;&lt;addDefaultImplementationEntries&gt;true&lt;/addDefaultImplementationEntries&gt;&#010;         &lt;mainClass&gt;main-class-name&lt;/mainClass&gt;&#010;         &lt;addClasspath&gt;true&lt;/addClasspath&gt;&#010;         &lt;classpathPrefix&gt;lib/&lt;/classpathPrefix&gt;&#010;       &lt;/manifest&gt;&#010;     &lt;/archive&gt;&#010;   &lt;/configuration&gt;&#010;&lt;/plugin&gt;&#010;&#010;2. Use the maven-dependency-plugin to copy over the libraries&#010;&#010;&lt;plugin&gt;&#010;   &lt;groupId&gt;org.apache.maven.plugins&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;   &lt;artifactId&gt;maven-dependency-plugin&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;   &lt;version&gt;2.8&lt;/version&gt;&#010;   &lt;executions&gt;&#010;     &lt;execution&gt;&#010;       &lt;phase&gt;package&lt;/phase&gt;&#010;       &lt;goals&gt;&#010;         &lt;goal&gt;copy-dependencies&lt;/goal&gt;&#010;       &lt;/goals&gt;&#010;       &lt;configuration&gt;&#010;&lt;outputDirectory&gt;${project.build.directory}/lib&lt;/outputDirectory&gt;&#010;         &lt;includeScope&gt;compile&lt;/includeScope&gt;&#010;       &lt;/configuration&gt;&#010;     &lt;/execution&gt;&#010;   &lt;/executions&gt;&#010;&lt;/plugin&gt;&#010;&#010;3. Run from the command line to test&#010;&#010;mvn package&#010;cd target&#010;java -jar jarFileName.jar&#010;&#010;To ship the binaries, use the maven-assembly-plugin and package both the &#010;JAR and the supporting libraries. That way when someone unpacks the zip &#010;(or tar or tar.gz, etc.), the directory structure will be maintained.&#010;&#010;Here's an assembly.xml file. I've left out the xml namespace declarations:&#010;&#010;&lt;?xml version="1.0" encoding="UTF-8"?&gt;&#010;&lt;assembly&gt;&#010;     &lt;id&gt;bin&lt;/id&gt;&#010;     &lt;formats&gt;&#010;         &lt;format&gt;tar.gz&lt;/format&gt;&#010;         &lt;format&gt;zip&lt;/format&gt;&#010;     &lt;/formats&gt;&#010;     &lt;includeBaseDirectory&gt;false&lt;/includeBaseDirectory&gt;&#010;     &lt;includeSiteDirectory&gt;false&lt;/includeSiteDirectory&gt;&#010;     &lt;fileSets&gt;&#010;         &lt;fileSet&gt;&#010;             &lt;directory&gt;target&lt;/directory&gt;&#010;             &lt;outputDirectory&gt;&lt;/outputDirectory&gt;&#010;             &lt;includes&gt;&#010;                 &lt;include&gt;*.jar&lt;/include&gt;&#010;                 &lt;include&gt;lib/&lt;/include&gt;&#010;             &lt;/includes&gt;&#010;         &lt;/fileSet&gt;&#010;     &lt;/fileSets&gt;&#010;&lt;/assembly&gt;&#010;&#010;Other ways include creating an uber-jar.&#010;&#010;. . . . just my two cents.&#010;/mde/&#010;&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

On 2/5/2014 11:40 AM, TenLeftFingers wrote:&#010;&gt; Hi Mark,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Thanks for that. I changed the pom as you suggested. When I ran with java&#010;&gt; -jar myApp.jar I got the output:&#010;&gt; *Failed to load Main-Class manifest attribute from target/myApp.jar*&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;A couple of things:&#010;&#010;1. the main-class-name was supposed to be your main class&#010;&#010;&gt; I opened the manifest and the *Main-Class* attribute was entered as&#010;&gt; *mainClass.* So I changed it to the former and that got rid of that error.&#010;&gt; But now  I *still *get the original error.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; The only pom change I'm not sure about is&#010;&gt; *&lt;classpathPrefix&gt;lib/&lt;/classpathPrefix&gt;*. What classes is that classpath&#010;&gt; trying to capture?&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;You need to change to the project target directory in order for it to &#010;run and find the supporting jars.&#010;&#010;The classpathPrefix line sets where to look for additional JAR files. It &#010;is relative to where you are.&#010;&#010;Maven compiles and packages your program into a JAR. It copies all of &#010;the supporting JAR files listed in your dependencies into target/lib.&#010;&#010;Before you run, make sure that target/lib exists and has all of the JAR &#010;files you need.&#010;&#010;Now, change to the target directory on the command line, and execute the &#010;program. The keys here are the following:&#010;&#010;1. change to the target directory on the command line&#010;2. execute the program with the following:&#010;&#010;java -jar my-app-1.0-SNAPSHOT.jar&#010;&#010;Now the lib directory will be in the correct relative path, and your &#010;dependencies should be found.&#010;&#010;&gt; Thanks,&#010;&gt; Ten&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;The exec plugin (http://mojo.codehaus.org/exec-maven-plugin/) as Wayne &#010;has mentioned is another way to accomplish this. This will help you run &#010;from within an IDE or by using mvn exec:exec, but it won't help you &#010;package and ship your code out for other users.&#010;&#010;You can combine both. I've not used the exec-maven-plugin, so creating &#010;the plugin configuration for that is left as an exercise for the reader. &#010;However, the documentation on the link listed above should get you started.&#010;&#010;/mde/&#010;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; On Wed, Feb 5, 2014 at 7:01 PM, Mark Eggers [via Maven] &lt;&#010;&gt; ml-node+s40175n5783298h15@n5.nabble.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; On 2/5/2014 9:52 AM, TenLeftFingers wrote:&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; When I build my Maven project with dependencies (using Netbeans but&#010;&gt;&gt; pointing&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; to a vanilla Maven installation), I get BUILD SUCCESS. Great!&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; When I try to /run /it in the form of *java -cp&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; target/my-app-1.0-SNAPSHOT.jar com.mycompany.app.App* I get this:&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; *java.lang.NoClassDefFoundError: org/slf4j/LoggerFactory*&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; How come this dependency fails at this late stage?&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; Trying to run the class from NetBeans itself gives a different error:&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; *Failed to execute goal org.codehaus.mojo:exec-maven-plugin:1.2.1:exec*&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; Please enlighten me as to how I can run this thing. It works fine in&#010;&gt;&gt; Eclipse&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; when I run it as a Java Application - but Eclipse has other problems&#010;&gt;&gt; that&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; I'm avoiding so I need to do this either from CLI or NetBeans&#010;&gt;&gt; (preferable).&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; Thanks,&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; Ten&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; I normally use NetBeans . . . .&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; One way to handle this (and it'll end up looking like a standard&#010;&gt;&gt; NetBeans project) is the following.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; 1. Modify the manifest via the maven-jar-plugin&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &lt;plugin&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;     &lt;groupId&gt;org.apache.maven.plugins&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;     &lt;artifactId&gt;maven-jar-plugin&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;     &lt;version&gt;2.4&lt;/version&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;     &lt;configuration&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;       &lt;archive&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;         &lt;manifest&#010;&gt;&gt; &lt;addDefaultImplementationEntries&gt;true&lt;/addDefaultImplementationEntries&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;           &lt;mainClass&gt;main-class-name&lt;/mainClass&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;           &lt;addClasspath&gt;true&lt;/addClasspath&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;           &lt;classpathPrefix&gt;lib/&lt;/classpathPrefix&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;         &lt;/manifest&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;       &lt;/archive&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;     &lt;/configuration&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &lt;/plugin&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; 2. Use the maven-dependency-plugin to copy over the libraries&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &lt;plugin&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;     &lt;groupId&gt;org.apache.maven.plugins&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;     &lt;artifactId&gt;maven-dependency-plugin&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;     &lt;version&gt;2.8&lt;/version&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;     &lt;executions&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;       &lt;execution&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;         &lt;phase&gt;package&lt;/phase&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;         &lt;goals&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;           &lt;goal&gt;copy-dependencies&lt;/goal&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;         &lt;/goals&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;         &lt;configuration&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &lt;outputDirectory&gt;${project.build.directory}/lib&lt;/outputDirectory&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;           &lt;includeScope&gt;compile&lt;/includeScope&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;         &lt;/configuration&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;       &lt;/execution&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;     &lt;/executions&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &lt;/plugin&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; 3. Run from the command line to test&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; mvn package&#010;&gt;&gt; cd target&#010;&gt;&gt; java -jar jarFileName.jar&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; To ship the binaries, use the maven-assembly-plugin and package both the&#010;&gt;&gt; JAR and the supporting libraries. That way when someone unpacks the zip&#010;&gt;&gt; (or tar or tar.gz, etc.), the directory structure will be maintained.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; Here's an assembly.xml file. I've left out the xml namespace declarations:&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &lt;?xml version="1.0" encoding="UTF-8"?&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &lt;assembly&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;       &lt;id&gt;bin&lt;/id&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;       &lt;formats&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;           &lt;format&gt;tar.gz&lt;/format&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;           &lt;format&gt;zip&lt;/format&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;       &lt;/formats&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;       &lt;includeBaseDirectory&gt;false&lt;/includeBaseDirectory&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;       &lt;includeSiteDirectory&gt;false&lt;/includeSiteDirectory&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;       &lt;fileSets&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;           &lt;fileSet&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;               &lt;directory&gt;target&lt;/directory&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;               &lt;outputDirectory&gt;&lt;/outputDirectory&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;               &lt;includes&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;                   &lt;include&gt;*.jar&lt;/include&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;                   &lt;include&gt;lib/&lt;/include&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;               &lt;/includes&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;           &lt;/fileSet&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;       &lt;/fileSets&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &lt;/assembly&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; Other ways include creating an uber-jar.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; . . . . just my two cents.&#010;&gt;&gt; /mde/&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

&gt; I added the maven-assembly-plugin as described here:&#010;&gt; http://stackoverflow.com/questions/574594/how-can-i-create-an-executable-jar-with-dependencies-using-maven&#010;&gt; and now the dependencies are bundled within the jar. Thanks for your help&#010;&#010;This is a fine approach. I still maintain the exec plugin is a great&#010;option for these types of uses - so long as you (the developer) are&#010;the one who needs to run the app. If you want to deliver it to a&#010;third-party in a single executable jar format, then assembly and other&#010;plugins are generally superior.&#010;&#010;Wayne&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Subject  :-
Best practices for Java EE 7 dependencies  
Date  :-
Fri, 07 Feb 2014 09:33:10 GMT  
contents:- 
Hi!&#010;&#010;I'm wondering what the best practices are for specifying Java EE 7&#010;dependencies in my modules.&#010;&#010;There is the so called BOM (bill of materials) POM: javax:javaee-api:7.0&#010;which lists all API submodules required for JEE7. Specifying this in my&#010;module as&#010;&#010;  &lt;dependency&gt;&#010;    &lt;groupId&gt;javax&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;    &lt;artifactId&gt;javaee-api&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;    &lt;version&gt;7.0&lt;/version&gt;&#010;  &lt;/dependency&gt;&#010;&#010;works and is the least work for me. However, this way I got all JEE APIs&#010;on the CLASSPATH even if I just need a few of them. Further on, the&#010;actual dependencies are now transitive which is (IMHO) not fully correct.&#010;Should I better specify the exact dependencies and investigate some more&#010;work in POM maintainance? What would this gain me?&#010;&#010;What do you think?&#010;&#010;- martin&#010;&#010;

Name  :- 
Thomas Broyer &lt;t.bro...@gmail.com&gt;  
Subject  :-
Re: Best practices for Java EE 7 dependencies  
Date  :-
Fri, 07 Feb 2014 17:03:44 GMT  
contents:- 
Because javax:javaee-api:7.0 doesn't use dependencyManagement, but declares&#010;straight dependencies, I don't think &lt;scope&gt;import&lt;/scope&gt; would work (or&#010;be appropriate); however you should be able to declare javax:javaee-api:1.0&#010;as a managed dependency (in &lt;dependencyManagement&gt;, but without any&#010;specific scope, i.e. &lt;scope&gt;compile&lt;/scope&gt; as it's the default) and then&#010;declare needed dependencies; I'm not sure that'd work either though. So I&#010;think the only real choice is to add it as a dependency, with&#010;&lt;scope&gt;provided&lt;/scope&gt;; you'll have all the JARs in the classpath at build&#010;time, but only at build time.&#010;&#010;&#010;On Fri, Feb 7, 2014 at 11:56 AM, Samuli Saarinen &lt;samuli.saarinen@remion.com&#010;&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; Hi,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; You could import the dependencies  in dependencyManagement as described in&#010;&gt; [1] and only declare needed dependencies in the project.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Cheers&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Samuli&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; [1]&#010;&gt; http://maven.apache.org/guides/introduction/introduction-to-dependency-mechanism.html#Importing_Dependencies&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; -----Original Message-----&#010;&gt; From: Martin Hoeller [mailto:martin@xss.co.at]&#010;&gt; Sent: 7. helmikuuta 2014 11:33&#010;&gt; To: Maven Users List&#010;&gt; Subject: Best practices for Java EE 7 dependencies&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Hi!&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I'm wondering what the best practices are for specifying Java EE 7&#010;&gt; dependencies in my modules.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; There is the so called BOM (bill of materials) POM: javax:javaee-api:7.0&#010;&gt; which lists all API submodules required for JEE7. Specifying this in my&#010;&gt; module as&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;   &lt;dependency&gt;&#010;&gt;     &lt;groupId&gt;javax&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;&gt;     &lt;artifactId&gt;javaee-api&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;&gt;     &lt;version&gt;7.0&lt;/version&gt;&#010;&gt;   &lt;/dependency&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; works and is the least work for me. However, this way I got all JEE APIs&#010;&gt; on the CLASSPATH even if I just need a few of them. Further on, the&#010;&gt; actual dependencies are now transitive which is (IMHO) not fully correct.&#010;&gt; Should I better specify the exact dependencies and investigate some more&#010;&gt; work in POM maintainance? What would this gain me?&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; What do you think?&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; - martin&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;-- &#010;Thomas Broyer&#010;/tɔ.ma.bʁwa.je/ &lt;http://xn--nna.ma.xn--bwa-xxb.je/&gt;&#010;&#010;

maven-ear-plugin silently overrides libraries  
Date  :-
Fri, 07 Feb 2014 14:21:54 GMT  
contents:- 
Hi there,&#010;&#010;I built an ear using the maven-ear-plugin (version 2.6).&#010;&#010;The ear is configured such that it includes two libraries into the lib&#010;folder, both with the same artifactId as well as the same version, but a&#010;different groupId. Now if I simply call 'mvn package' only the first one is&#010;included, but no warning whatsoever appears. Only once I turn on debugging&#010;(mvn --debug package), I see one subtle message:&#010;[DEBUG] Skipping artifact [jar:com.foo:bar:1.0] as it is already up to date&#010;at [lib/bar-1.0.jar]&#010;&#010;Wouldn't it make sense to either include the groupId in the filename or at&#010;least make a check (that includes the groupId) beforehand if there are any&#010;conflicts?&#010;&#010;Cheers,&#010;Reto&#010;&#010;

Name  :- 
Ron Wheeler &lt;rwhee...@artifact-software.com&gt;  
Subject  :-
Re: maven-ear-plugin silently overrides libraries  
Date  :-
Fri, 07 Feb 2014 14:33:57 GMT  
contents:- 
If your IDE supports Maven (Eclipse/STS for example), you will see the &#010;conflict in the dependency hierarchy view and you can fix it with the &#010;right exclusions.&#010;&#010;It is almost always worth a quick look through the dependency hierarchy &#010;view if you use a lot of third party libraries.&#010;Not everyone updates their dependencies when they build a shareable library.&#010;You can sometimes get some pretty old versions of things dragged in with &#010;the latest version of otherwise well-written libraries.&#010;Exclusions need to be added to get what you want in your artifacts.&#010;&#010;Ron&#010;&#010;On 07/02/2014 9:21 AM, Reto Hablützel wrote:&#010;&gt; Hi there,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I built an ear using the maven-ear-plugin (version 2.6).&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; The ear is configured such that it includes two libraries into the lib&#010;&gt; folder, both with the same artifactId as well as the same version, but a&#010;&gt; different groupId. Now if I simply call 'mvn package' only the first one is&#010;&gt; included, but no warning whatsoever appears. Only once I turn on debugging&#010;&gt; (mvn --debug package), I see one subtle message:&#010;&gt; [DEBUG] Skipping artifact [jar:com.foo:bar:1.0] as it is already up to date&#010;&gt; at [lib/bar-1.0.jar]&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Wouldn't it make sense to either include the groupId in the filename or at&#010;&gt; least make a check (that includes the groupId) beforehand if there are any&#010;&gt; conflicts?&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Cheers,&#010;&gt; Reto&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;&#010;-- &#010;Ron Wheeler&#010;President&#010;Artifact Software Inc&#010;email: rwheeler@artifact-software.com&#010;skype: ronaldmwheeler&#010;phone: 866-970-2435, ext 102&#010;&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Name  :- 
Ron Wheeler &lt;rwhee...@artifact-software.com&gt;  
Subject  :-
Re: maven-ear-plugin silently overrides libraries  
Date  :-
Fri, 07 Feb 2014 16:04:53 GMT  
contents:- 
Exclusions will not help in this case.&#010;Looking through the dependency hierarchy will at least get you to see &#010;the problem earlier which I think was the nature of your question.&#010;&#010;It appears from my brief reading and fun with making servlets run in &#010;production that classloaders merge classes by name.&#010;Maven does not.&#010;&#010;I am a bit surprised that groupId does not count.&#010;&#010;If one uses a lot of third -party libraries, it would seem inevitable &#010;that you could need com.artifact-software:utilities:1.0 at the same time &#010;as ch.rethab:utilities:1.0 at the same time.&#010;The classloader is not going to cause any problem but if Maven throws &#010;out one of these as a duplicate, you will be missing classes at run-time.&#010;&#010;It is difficult to force everyone to create unique artifactIds unless &#010;you get rid of the GroupId altogther and make GAV -&gt; &lt;AV&gt; and put the &#010;group name into the artifactID.&#010;&#010;This seems to be a design flaw if it is true.&#010;&#010;Ron&#010;&#010;On 07/02/2014 9:43 AM, Reto Hablützel wrote:&#010;&gt; Sure, but exclusions don't do the trick if you need both of them, do &#010;&gt; they? I am talking about completely independent libraries that happen &#010;&gt; to have the same artifactId.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Those were actually both libraries of mine and I could obviously fix &#010;&gt; this issue rather simply, but I was just thinking that it would be &#010;&gt; helpful to have at least a warning or something from maven - &#010;&gt; regardless of the IDE.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; - Reto&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; On Fri, Feb 7, 2014 at 3:33 PM, Ron Wheeler &#010;&gt; &lt;rwheeler@artifact-software.com &#010;&gt; &lt;mailto:rwheeler@artifact-software.com&gt;&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;     If your IDE supports Maven (Eclipse/STS for example), you will see&#010;&gt;     the conflict in the dependency hierarchy view and you can fix it&#010;&gt;     with the right exclusions.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;     It is almost always worth a quick look through the dependency&#010;&gt;     hierarchy view if you use a lot of third party libraries.&#010;&gt;     Not everyone updates their dependencies when they build a&#010;&gt;     shareable library.&#010;&gt;     You can sometimes get some pretty old versions of things dragged&#010;&gt;     in with the latest version of otherwise well-written libraries.&#010;&gt;     Exclusions need to be added to get what you want in your artifacts.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;     Ron&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;     On 07/02/2014 9:21 AM, Reto Hablützel wrote:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;         Hi there,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;         I built an ear using the maven-ear-plugin (version 2.6).&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;         The ear is configured such that it includes two libraries into&#010;&gt;         the lib&#010;&gt;         folder, both with the same artifactId as well as the same&#010;&gt;         version, but a&#010;&gt;         different groupId. &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; &gt; It is difficult to force everyone to create unique artifactIds unless&#010;&gt;&gt; you&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; &gt; get rid of the GroupId altogther and make GAV -&gt; &lt;AV&gt; and put&#010;the&#010;&gt;&gt; group&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; &gt; name into the artifactID.&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; &gt; This seems to be a design flaw if it is true.&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; contents:- 
&gt; Date: Sat, 8 Feb 2014 09:59:27 -0800&#010;&gt; From: desmond.kirrane@gmail.com&#010;&gt; To: users@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt; Subject: Reload MavenProject MavenSession and BuildPluginManager&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; How can my Moo reload/refresh MavenProject MavenSession and&#010;&gt; BuildPluginManager components.&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; I need to do this after my Mojo switches the a different Git branch.&#010;MG&gt;so you have a "new feature branch"&#010;MG&gt;git hf feature start ##feature name## &#010;&#010;MG&gt;I would set this as a post-create task on a Hudson job  e.g.&#010;MG&gt;and implement 'git hf feature #feature name#' on post-create of Hudson Job&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; --&#010;&gt; View this message in context: http://maven.40175.n5.nabble.com/Reload-MavenProject-MavenSession-and-BuildPluginManager-tp5783698.html&#010;&gt; Sent from the Maven - Users mailing list archive at Nabble.com.&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; ---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;&gt; To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt; For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt; &#010; &#009;&#009; &#009;   &#009;&#009;  &#010;

contents:- 
you will need to trigger ArtifactResolver.resolveAlways with the artifact, localRepository&#010;properly populated for each of the requested artifacts..Here is an example from maven-netbeans-plugin&#010;&#010; &#010;&#010;private void resolve(Artifact artifact, boolean failOnError, boolean remote) throws MojoExecutionException&#010;{ &#010;&#010;129.        if (!artifact.isResolved() || artifact.isSnapshot()) { &#010;130.            try { &#010;131.                artifactResolver.resolveAlways(artifact, remote ? remoteArtifactRepositories&#010;: Collections.EMPTY_LIST, localRepository); &#010;132.            } catch (AbstractArtifactResolutionException ex) { &#010;133.                if (failOnError) { &#010;134.                    throw new MojoExecutionException("can not resolve " + artifact, ex);&#010;&#010;135.                } &#010;136.            } &#010;137.        } &#010;138.    }&#010;&#010;https://kenai.com/projects/mvn-nb-plugin/sources/subversion/content/src/main/java/com/kenai/maven/netbeans/plugin/NetBeansMojo.java?rev=4&#010;&#010;Martin &#010;______________________________________________ &#010;&#010;  &#010;&#010;&#010;&gt; Date: Sat, 8 Feb 2014 09:59:27 -0800&#010;&gt; From: desmond.kirrane@gmail.com&#010;&gt; To: users@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt; Subject: Reload MavenProject MavenSession and BuildPluginManager&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; How can my Moo reload/refresh MavenProject MavenSession and&#010;&gt; BuildPluginManager components.&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; I need to do this after my Mojo switches the a different Git branch.&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; --&#010;&gt; View this message in context: http://maven.40175.n5.nabble.com/Reload-MavenProject-MavenSession-and-BuildPluginManager-tp5783698.html&#010;&gt; Sent from the Maven - Users mailing list archive at Nabble.com.&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; ---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;&gt; To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt; For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt; &#010; &#009;&#009; &#009;   &#009;&#009;  &#010;

Michael Osipov &lt;micha...@apache.org&gt;  
Subject  :-
Re: wsimport - catalog  
Date  :-
Mon, 10 Feb 2014 20:49:08 GMT  
contents:- 
Am 2014-02-10 21:28, schrieb Zmuda, Matt:&#010;&gt; Hi All,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I am trying to generate some web service client code from a WSDL and schemas that I have.&#010;&gt; One issue I am encountering is that one schema file (xsd) I require is in a separate&#010;jar that my client project has a dependency on.&#010;&gt; I cannot figure out how to reference that file in my pom. I have been lead down the path&#010;of looking into defining a catalog (and it seems that how it was done in the and build we&#010;use to use) however I can't get this working.&#010;&#010;That is not a Maven problem but simply a configuration problem with the &#010;JAX-WS Maven Plugin.&#010;&#010;In this case, you should work like this:&#010;&#010;Parent&#010;|- JAR with generated classes from the XSD with generated episode file&#010;|- JAR with SEI and provided episode file, wsimport won't duplicate the &#010;model in that case.&#010;&#010;Generally, the JAX-WS Plugin has a few shortcomings compared to the JAXB &#010;plugin. Search the JAX_WS_COMMONS JIRA and you'll find the tickets.&#010;&#010;Michael&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Thank you.&#010;[ERROR] java.lang.AssertionError: typeSig 19&#010;[ERROR] at&#010;com.sun.tools.javac.jvm.ClassWriter.assembleSig(ClassWriter.java:357)&#010;[ERROR] at com.sun.tools.javac.jvm.ClassWriter.typeSig(ClassWriter.java:424)&#010;...&#010;&#010;In attempting to identify the cause, I started by just adding dependency&#010;management to my parent pom&#010;Simply adding  &#010;&lt;dependencyManagement&gt;&#010;&lt;/dependencyManagement&gt;&#010;around the dependencies in my parent pom, causes dependencies not be&#010;resolved&#010;&#010;Does anyone have any idea why using dependency management might cause&#010;compilation errors&#010; - or why just adding dependency management to the parent pom would cause&#010;dependency resolution errors&#010; &#010;Thanks for reading and any help&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;--&#010;View this message in context: http://maven.40175.n5.nabble.com/Adding-dependency-management-to-parent-pom-causes-errors-tp5784035.html&#010;Sent from the Maven - Users mailing list archive at Nabble.com.&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Name  :- 
Laird Nelson &lt;ljnel...@gmail.com&gt;  
Subject  :-
Re: Adding dependency management to parent pom causes errors  
Date  :-
Tue, 11 Feb 2014 23:47:32 GMT  
contents:- 
On Tue, Feb 11, 2014 at 12:18 AM, geoffh &lt;hartnell_g@yahoo.co.uk&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; In attempting to identify the cause, I started by just adding dependency&#010;&gt;&#010;management to my parent pom&#010;&gt; Simply adding&#010;&gt; &lt;dependencyManagement&gt;&#010;&gt; &lt;/dependencyManagement&gt;&#010;&gt; around the dependencies in my parent pom, causes dependencies not be&#010;&gt; resolved&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;I'm not sure why the developers chose the words "dependency management" to&#010;identify the particular XML section in question.  It's very confusing.&#010;&#010;Think of the &lt;dependencyManagement&gt; section as serving two purposes.&#010;&#010;First, and foremost, it is template information.  If a given real&#010;&lt;dependency&gt; somewhere else omits a piece of information, then that piece&#010;of information is taken (if possible) from the &lt;dependencyManagement&gt;&#010;section.&#010;&#010;Second, which is really an outgrowth of the first, it constrains the&#010;versions of transitive dependencies that might be pulled in from somewhere&#010;else.  I say this is an outgrowth of the first concern, because strictly&#010;speaking your project never mentions a transitive dependency, so that&#010;"piece of information" is missing just like, say, a version string.&#010;&#010;Note as well that the stuff in the &lt;dependencyManagement&gt; section can be&#010;made up.  That is, you can put dependency management elements in there that&#010;don't actually pick out any dependencies in the world.  See my earlier&#010;point about this being a template area.&#010;&#010;Putting this all together, it still follows that you have to have *real*&#010;dependencies defined.  If you simply wrap your "real" dependencies with&#010;&lt;dependencyManagement&gt;&lt;/dependencyManagement&gt;, that is clearly not going to&#010;work: you've now specified a template, but nothing that the template will&#010;be merged into.&#010;&#010;The compilation error you're talking about looks like something more&#010;substantial than a bad dependency--you're getting a compiler error from&#010;within javac itself.&#010;&#010;I noticed that "-gwt" showed up in some of your artifact names; perhaps&#010;something with GWT is not playing nice.&#010;&#010;Hope something in here helps.&#010;&#010;Best,&#010;Laird&#010;&#010;-- &#010;http://about.me/lairdnelson&#010;&#010;

Name  :- 
Barrie Treloar &lt;baerr...@gmail.com&gt;  
Subject  :-
Re: Adding dependency management to parent pom causes errors  
Date  :-
Wed, 12 Feb 2014 00:48:36 GMT  
contents:- 
On 12 February 2014 10:17, Laird Nelson &lt;ljnelson@gmail.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt; First, and foremost, it is template information.  If a given real&#010;&gt; &lt;dependency&gt; somewhere else omits a piece of information, then that piece&#010;&gt; of information is taken (if possible) from the &lt;dependencyManagement&gt;&#010;&gt; section.&#010;&#010;This is also best practice.&#010;&#010;Appliying DRY principles you pull up all the dependency information&#010;from your child poms into your parent pom's dependencyManagement&#010;section.&#010;Then in your child poms you *always* omit the version information in&#010;your dependency section.&#010;&#010;This way you know that your project is using a consistent version of artifacts.&#010;The last thing you want is for your project to be using a mish-mash of&#010;GWT versions (1.0 in one project, 2.6 in another, etc).&#010;&#010;This gives you one place to define the versions.&#010;And when its time to upgrade then one place to make the change.&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Wed, 12 Feb 2014 01:21:57 GMT

On Tue, Feb 11, 2014 at 4:48 PM, Barrie Treloar &lt;baerrach@gmail.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; This is also best practice.&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;Agreed wholesale.  I think the original poster was wondering why this&#010;stanza:&#010;&#010;&lt;dependencies&gt;&#010;&lt;!-- ... --&gt;&#010;&lt;/dependencies&gt;&#010;&#010;&#010;...when "wrapped" (replaced, really) thusly:&#010;&#010;*&lt;dependencyManagement&gt;*&#010;  &lt;dependencies&gt;&#010;  &lt;!-- ... --&gt;&#010;  &lt;/dependencies&gt;&#010;*&lt;/dependencyManagement&gt;*&#010;&#010;&#010;...suddenly {handwave handwave} made his dependencies stop {handwave}&#010;resolving.  (The answer being of course that there is no longer a&#010;&lt;dependencies&gt; section in this particular case; he replaced it—did not&#010;augment it—with a &lt;dependencyManagement&gt; stanza.)&#010;&#010;While we're on the subject of best practices in this area, we've also found&#010;that dependency managing the versions of even child &lt;modules&gt; pays off in&#010;the end.&#010;&#010;Best,&#010;Laird&#010;&#010;-- &#010;http://about.me/lairdnelson&#010;&#010;

On 12 February 2014 11:51, Laird Nelson &lt;ljnelson@gmail.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt; Agreed wholesale.  I think the original poster was wondering why this&#010;&gt; stanza:&#010;[del]&#010;&#010;You did a good job there so I didn't add any value to the response.&#010;&#010;&gt; While we're on the subject of best practices in this area, we've also found&#010;&gt; that dependency managing the versions of even child &lt;modules&gt; pays off in&#010;&gt; the end.&#010;&#010;Be careful here.&#010;People get confused with what a module is.&#010;&#010;A module is not a dependency.&#010;I think of it as a handy shortcut to allow me to run a maven command&#010;at the top and have the same command also run in any module&#010;declaration.&#010;Logically a module is a group of things that tend to get released&#010;together. If that is not the case, then don't use a module.&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Hi,&#010;&#010;DependencyManagement is declaring dependencies(mostly for versions) and&#010;dependencies is using them,&#010;So in general you should have only dependencyManagement in the parent poms&#010;and only dependencies in the childs.&#010;&#010;Now there are exceptions, for example junit is generally used in all child&#010;projects , so you can add it in dependencies of the parent pom and it will&#010;be avaible in all childs.&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;On Wed, Feb 12, 2014 at 10:33 AM, geoffh &lt;hartnell_g@yahoo.co.uk&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; Laird, Barrie&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Thanks for taking the time with some useful explanations&#010;&gt; I'd like to put more detail into my problem in the hope that you may be&#010;&gt; Name  :- 
Barrie Treloar &lt;baerr...@gmail.com&gt;  
Subject  :-
Re: Adding dependency management to parent pom causes errors  
Date  :-
Wed, 12 Feb 2014 14:09:30 GMT  
contents:- 
On 12 February 2014 20:12, Adrien Rivard &lt;adrien.rivard@gmail.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt; Hi,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; DependencyManagement is declaring dependencies(mostly for versions) and&#010;&gt; dependencies is using them,&#010;&gt; So in general you should have only dependencyManagement in the parent poms&#010;&gt; and only dependencies in the childs.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Now there are exceptions, for example junit is generally used in all child&#010;&gt; projects , so you can add it in dependencies of the parent pom and it will&#010;&gt; be avaible in all childs.&#010;&#010;Adding dependencies into the pom with modules is a bad idea,&#010;There will always be an exception that breaks that rule.&#010;Then you will be asking how do I remove a dependency from a child pom&#010;- you can't, dont define it in the first place.&#010;&#010;Typical exceptions would be poms whose sole purpose is to build an&#010;assembly (zip file) for package management, or Ear poms, etc.&#010;&#010;A best practice is to never have any dependencies in a pom that has modules.&#010;If you want to share common dependencies between projects, then you&#010;can look at using the inherit type relationship but that pom would be&#010;a standalone pom with no module declarations.&#010;Your top level project is an Aggregation pom to make running Maven easier.&#010;See https://maven.apache.org/pom.html#Aggregation&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Why is dependency:analyze lying to me?  
Date  :-

contents:- 
Hi,&#010;&#010;I’m using Maven 3.1.1 on Mac 10.9.1.  When I ran “mvn dependency:analyze” on&#010;my project, I got results that included:&#010;&#010;&#009;[WARNING] Unused declared dependencies found:&#010;&#009;…&#010;&#009;[WARNING]    junit:junit:jar:4.11:test&#010;&#010;So I commented out the above junit dependency in my pom (declared like so):&#010;&#010;                &lt;dependency&gt;&#010;                        &lt;groupId&gt;junit&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;                        &lt;artifactId&gt;junit&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;                        &lt;version&gt;${version.junit}&lt;/version&gt;&#010;                        &lt;scope&gt;test&lt;/scope&gt;&#010;                &lt;/dependency&gt;&#010;&#010;However, when I ran “mvm clean install” on my project, I got errors like&#010;&#010;&#009;initializationError0(org.mainco.subco.core.SerializableTest)  Time elapsed:&#010;0 sec  &lt;&lt;&lt; ERROR!&#010;&#009;java.lang.NoSuchFieldError: NULL&#010;&#009;&#009;at org.junit.runners.ParentRunner.&lt;init&gt;(ParentRunner.java:48)&#010;&#009;&#009;at&#010;org.junit.runners.BlockJUnit4ClassRunner.&lt;init&gt;(BlockJUnit4ClassRunner.java:58)&#010;&#009;&#009;at&#010;org.springframework.test.context.junit4.SpringJUnit4ClassRunner.&lt;init&gt;(SpringJUnit4ClassRunner.java:104)&#010;&#010;This isn’t the only dependency that the analyze goal lists that wreaks havoc&#010;when I comment it out. On 12 February 2014 07:41, laredotornado-3 &lt;laredotornado@gmail.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt; Hi,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I'm using Maven 3.1.1 on Mac 10.9.1.  When I ran "mvn dependency:analyze" on&#010;&gt; my project, I got results that included:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;         [WARNING] Unused declared dependencies found:&#010;&gt;         ...&#010;&gt;         [WARNING]    junit:junit:jar:4.11:test&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; So I commented out the above junit dependency in my pom (declared like so):&#010;[del]&#010;&gt;         java.lang.NoSuchFieldError: NULL&#010;&gt;                 at org.junit.runners.ParentRunner.&lt;init&gt;(ParentRunner.java:48)&#010;&gt;                 at&#010;&gt; org.junit.runners.BlockJUnit4ClassRunner.&lt;init&gt;(BlockJUnit4ClassRunner.java:58)&#010;&gt;                 at&#010;&gt; org.springframework.test.context.junit4.SpringJUnit4ClassRunner.&lt;init&gt;(SpringJUnit4ClassRunner.java:104)&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; This isn't the only dependency that the analyze goal lists that wreaks havoc&#010;&gt; when I comment it out.  Is there another way to detect what dependencies are&#010;&gt; truly not needed by my project?&#010;&#010;Unfortunately this stuff is not documented well enough in the plugin.&#010;You're welcome to submit a patch!&#010;&#010;Have a look at http://maven.apache.org/plugins/maven-dependency-plugin/faq.html#unused&#010;&#010;I think Maven is missing a scope, it needs to break up test into two&#010;phases; testCompile and testRuntime instead of having one scope which&#010;means both.&#010;This means that the analyze code can't tell what stuff is needed for&#010;tests at compile time and what is needed at runtime.&#010;&#010;If my memory serves me right, that would mean for your example that&#010;Spring is a compile time dependency but junit would be a runtime&#010;dependency.&#010;Hence the incorrect "Unused declared dependencies found" error.&#010;&#010;I would manually ignore anything found in the test scope from the error list.&#010;I never found the time to go hacking the plugin to work better - i.e.&#010;if it is test scope it really can't tell the difference between unused&#010;dependencies and shouldn't report them.&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;
