I am so happy someone brought this up. I actually hit this issue several&#010;times but never got around to mentioning it. Please submit a JIRA issue!&#010;&#010;&#010;On Tue, Feb 11, 2014 at 3:41 PM, Barrie Treloar &lt;baerrach@gmail.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; On 12 February 2014 07:41, laredotornado-3 &lt;laredotornado@gmail.com&gt;&#010;&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt; &gt; Hi,&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; I'm using Maven 3.1.1 on Mac 10.9.1.  When I ran "mvn&#010;&gt; dependency:analyze" on&#010;&gt; &gt; my project, I got results that included:&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;         [WARNING] Unused declared dependencies found:&#010;&gt; &gt;         ...&#010;&gt; &gt;         [WARNING]    junit:junit:jar:4.11:test&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; So I commented out the above junit dependency in my pom (declared like&#010;&gt; so):&#010;&gt; [del]&#010;&gt; &gt;         java.lang.NoSuchFieldError: NULL&#010;&gt; &gt;                 at&#010;&gt; org.junit.runners.ParentRunner.&lt;init&gt;(ParentRunner.java:48)&#010;&gt; &gt;                 at&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; org.junit.runners.BlockJUnit4ClassRunner.&lt;init&gt;(BlockJUnit4ClassRunner.java:58)&#010;&gt; &gt;                 at&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; org.springframework.test.context.junit4.SpringJUnit4ClassRunner.&lt;init&gt;(SpringJUnit4ClassRunner.java:104)&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; This isn't the only dependency that the analyze goal lists that wreaks&#010;&gt; havoc&#010;&gt; &gt; when I comment it out.  Is there another way to detect what dependencies&#010;&gt; are&#010;&gt; &gt; truly not needed by my project?&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Unfortunately this stuff is not documented well enough in the plugin.&#010;&gt; You're welcome to submit a patch!&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Have a look at&#010;&gt; http://maven.apache.org/plugins/maven-dependency-plugin/faq.html#unused&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I think Maven is missing a scope, it needs to break up test into two&#010;&gt; phases; testCompile and testRuntime instead of having one scope which&#010;&gt; means both.&#010;&gt; This means that the analyze code can't tell what stuff is needed for&#010;&gt; tests at compile time and what is needed at runtime.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; If my memory serves me right, that would mean for your example that&#010;&gt; Spring is a compile time dependency but junit would be a runtime&#010;&gt; dependency.&#010;&gt; Hence the incorrect "Unused declared dependencies found" error.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I would manually ignore anything found in the test scope from the error&#010;&gt; list.&#010;&gt; I never found the time to go hacking the plugin to work better - i.e.&#010;&gt; if it is test scope it really can't tell the difference between unused&#010;&gt; dependencies and shouldn't report them.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; ---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;&gt; To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt; For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;&#010;-- &#010;Cheers,&#010;Paul&#010;&#010;

On Wed, Feb 12, 2014 at 08:11:29AM +1030, Barrie Treloar wrote:&#010;[snip]&#010;&gt; I think Maven is missing a scope, it needs to break up test into two&#010;&gt; phases; testCompile and testRuntime instead of having one scope which&#010;&gt; means both.&#010;&gt; This means that the analyze code can't tell what stuff is needed for&#010;&gt; tests at compile time and what is needed at runtime.&#010;&#010;Picky terminology tweak:  I went off to check my memory because I was&#010;*sure* that Maven has a full set of test-* phases parallel to what we&#010;might call the "main" phases.  It has.  Then I came back here and saw&#010;that what you want is parallel *scopes* [test]Compile, [test]Runtime.&#010;&#010;Having sorted that (I hope), I think I agree with you.&#010;&#010;-- &#010;Mark H. Wood, Lead System Programmer   mwood@IUPUI.Edu&#010;Machines should not be friendly.  Machines should be obedient.&#010;&#010;

Especially if you use Spring XML configuration, it's impossible for the&#010;Dependency Plugin to figure out you need this-or-that Spring jar. The best&#010;you can do, actually, is use the new Spring Java Config so that your&#010;configuration is code and thus able to be statically analyzed.&#010;&#010;&#010;On Thu, Feb 13, 2014 at 3:54 PM, laredotornado-3 &lt;laredotornado@gmail.com&gt;wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; org.apache.jasper.compiler.ErrorDispatcher.jspError(ErrorDispatcher.java:116)&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; because the JSP includes this&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;         &lt;%@ taglib prefix="sec"&#010;&gt; uri="http://www.springframework.org/security/tags"%&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; This may fall into the “How the hell is Maven supposed to know?” category,&#010;&#010;Yes, it most certainly does.&#010;&#010;&gt; [WARNING]&#010;&gt; org.springframework.security:spring-security-taglibs:jar:3.1.1.RELEASE:compile&#010;...&#010;&gt; Anyway, not sure if the plugin can be configured to detect these kind of&#010;&gt; things, but a guy can dream, can’t he??&#010;&#010;You would need to write code that performs the following tasks:&#010;1. look in jar files related to dependencies&#010;2. find taglib files and other configuration files [each file type&#010;needs its own parser]&#010;3. store tag uris that are discovered along with the associated jar&#010;4. check those tag uris vs what is in your code (keep in mind some may&#010;be in config files you wrote, so gotta parse those too - more code to&#010;write)&#010;5. output the list of jars (dependencies) which are not actually used&#010;in code or config&#010;&#010;This is nontrivial, so no one has done it. And there is your problem.&#010;&gt; You have an _ in your groupid for the artifact, but not your include filter.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I've been looking at maven-common-artifact-filters-1.4&#010;&gt; PatternIncludesArtifactFilter.matchAgainst(). since I thought that may&#010;&gt; you needed a trailing : on the long id.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; But it does the "right thing" with as much of the pattern you provide&#010;&gt; - and wildcards the rest.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; ---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;&gt; Code coverage with debug logs: 100% branch coverage not possible?...  
Date  :-
Wed, 12 Feb 2014 20:30:52 GMT  
contents:- 
Hi all,&#010;&#010; &#010;&#010;I need your opinion/way to tackle the following problem:&#010;&#010;In many projects we use a Logger (doesnt matter which implementation). It&#010;is often recommend to test if the debug level is activated before logging a&#010;debug trace like the following:&#010;&#010;if (logger.isDebugEnabled()) {&#010;&#010;    logger.debug(blah  + i +  in the loop that contains  + max);&#010;&#010;}&#010;&#010; &#010;&#010;Now when you run unit tests on this kind of code you need to make a choice:&#010;run tests with INFO level or run tests with ALL traces activated. I choose&#010;the second option in order to:&#010;&#010;*         Check that debug traces doesnt throw unwanted exception (like&#010;NPE)&#010;&#010;*         Have a better code coverage in term of covered lines&#010;&#010; &#010;&#010;But in term of branches coverage we could never have a 100% :(&#010;&#010; &#010;&#010;To me the only way to cover this is to run the tests suite 2 times: one with&#010;INFO traces configured, and another one with ALL traces activated.&#010;&#010;Did you face this issue and how did you solve it ?&#010;&#010; &#010;&#010;Thanks,&#010;&#010;Benoît.&#010;&#010;&#010;

Name  :- 
Paul Benedict &lt;pbened...@apache.org&gt;  
Subject  :-
Re: Code coverage with debug logs: 100% branch coverage not possible?...  
Date  :-
Wed, 12 Feb 2014 20:36:27 GMT  
contents:- 
IIRC, there should be an option in Emma/Cobertura that allows you to&#010;exclude coverage on certain classes. So if you can exclude your log4j&#010;classes (you don't really want to test your logging, do you?), then you&#010;should be able to raise your percentage.&#010;&#010;&#010;On Wed, Feb 12, 2014 at 2:30 PM, Benoît Berthonneau&#010;&lt;benoit@berthonneau.com&gt;wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; Hi all,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I need your opinion/way to tackle the following problem:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; In many projects we use a Logger (doesn't matter which implementation). It&#010;&gt; is often recommend to test if the debug level is activated before logging a&#010;&gt; debug trace like the following:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; if (logger.isDebugEnabled()) {&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;     logger.debug("blah " + i + " in the loop that contains " + max);&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; }&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Now when you run unit tests on this kind of code you need to make a choice:&#010;&gt; run tests with INFO level or run tests with ALL traces activated. I choose&#010;&gt; the second option in order to:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; *         Check that debug traces doesn't throw unwanted exception (like&#010;&gt; NPE)&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; *         Have a better code coverage in term of covered lines&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; But in term of branches coverage we could never have a 100% :(&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; To me the only way to cover this is to run the tests suite 2 times: one&#010;&gt; with&#010;&gt; INFO traces configured, and another one with ALL traces activated.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Did you face this issue and how did you solve it ?&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Thanks,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Benoît.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;&#010;-- &#010;Cheers,&#010;Paul&#010;&#010;

I &#010;&#010;&gt; choose the second option in order to:&#010;&#010;&gt; &#010;&#010;&gt; *         Check that debug traces doesn't throw unwanted exception (like&#010;&#010;&gt; NPE)&#010;&#010;&gt; &#010;&#010;&gt; *         Have a better code coverage in term of covered lines&#010;&#010;&gt; &#010;&#010;&gt; &#010;&#010;&gt; &#010;&#010;&gt; But in term of branches coverage we could never have a 100% :(&#010;&#010;&gt; &#010;&#010;&gt; &#010;&#010;&gt; &#010;&#010;&gt; To me the only way to cover this is to run the tests suite 2 times: &#010;&#010;&gt; one with INFO traces configured, and another one with ALL traces &#010;&#010;&gt; activated.&#010;&#010;&gt; &#010;&#010;&gt; Did you face this issue and how did you solve it ?&#010;&#010;&gt; &#010;&#010;&gt; &#010;&#010;&gt; &#010;&#010;&gt; Thanks,&#010;&#010;&gt; &#010;&#010;&gt; Benoît.&#010;&#010;&gt; &#010;&#010;&gt; &#010;&#010; &#010;&#010; &#010;&#010;--&#010;&#010;Cheers,&#010;&#010;Paul&#010;&#010;&#010;

RE: Code coverage with debug logs: 100% branch coverage not possible?...  
Date  :-
Wed, 12 Feb 2014 21:10:31 GMT  
contents:- 
It does matter which implementation.  The main reason it was recommended to&#010;check the logging level was because string concatenation can be expensive,&#010;and you want to avoid doing it for a message that won't be logged.  But if&#010;you're using a logging API like slf4j that uses parameter replacement&#010;tokens in the message string, if the message isn't logged, the replacement&#010;won't be performed and the call will be cheap.&#010;On Feb 12, 2014 1:57 PM, "Benoît Berthonneau" &lt;benoit@berthonneau.com&gt;&#010;wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; Hi Paul,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Don't think that I could play with exclusions. Here is an example :&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; *A Unit Test :*&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; *The tested class with ALL traces activated:*&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; *And the same tested class with INFO traces activated:*&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; -----Message d'origine-----&#010;&gt; De : paulus.benedictus@gmail.com [mailto:paulus.benedictus@gmail.com] De&#010;&gt; la part de Paul Benedict&#010;&gt; Envoyé : mercredi 12 février 2014 21:36&#010;&gt; À : Maven Users List&#010;&gt; Objet : Re: Code coverage with debug logs: 100% branch coverage not&#010;&gt; possible?...&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; IIRC, there should be an option in Emma/Cobertura that allows you to&#010;&gt; exclude coverage on certain classes. So if you can exclude your log4j&#010;&gt; classes (you don't really want to test your logging, do you?), then you&#010;&gt; should be able to raise your percentage.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; On Wed, Feb 12, 2014 at 2:30 PM, Benoît Berthonneau&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &lt;benoit@berthonneau.com&gt;wrote:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; Hi all,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; I need your opinion/way to tackle the following problem:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; In many projects we use a Logger (doesn't matter which&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; implementation). It is often recommend to test if the debug level is&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; activated before logging a debug trace like the following:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; if (logger.isDebugEnabled()) {&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;     logger.debug("blah " + i + " in the loop that contains " + max);&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; }&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; Now when you run unit tests on this kind of code you need to make a&#010;&gt; choice:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; run tests with INFO level or run tests with ALL traces activated. I&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; choose the second option in order to:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; *         Check that debug traces doesn't throw unwanted exception (like&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; NPE)&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; *         Have a better code coverage in term of covered lines&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; But in term of branches coverage we could never have a 100% :(&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; To me the only way to cover this is to run the tests suite 2 times:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; one with INFO traces configured, and another one with ALL traces&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; activated.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; Did you face this issue and how did you solve it ?&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; Thanks,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; Benoît.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; --&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Cheers,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Paul&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;

Hello Benoit,&#010;&#010;Kevin is right, using slf4j[0] one would use sth. like:&#010;&#010;logger.debug(“blah {} in the loop that contains {}”, i, max);&#010;&#010;No need for iffing :-).&#010;&#010;[0] http://www.slf4j.org/manual.html&#010;Regards Mirko&#010;--&#010;http://illegalstateexception.blogspot.com/&#010;https://github.com/mfriedenhagen/ (http://osrc.dfm.io/mfriedenhagen)&#010;https://bitbucket.org/mfriedenhagen/&#010;&#010;&#010;On Wed, Feb 12, 2014 at 10:10 PM, Kevin Krumwiede &lt;kjkrum@gmail.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt; It does matter which implementation.  The main reason it was recommended to&#010;&gt; check the logging level was because string concatenation can be expensive,&#010;&gt; and you want to avoid doing it for a message that won't be logged.  But if&#010;&gt; you're using a logging API like slf4j that uses parameter replacement&#010;&gt; tokens in the message string, if the message isn't logged, the replacement&#010;&gt; won't be performed and the call will be cheap.&#010;&gt; On Feb 12, 2014 1:57 PM, "Benoît Berthonneau" &lt;benoit@berthonneau.com&gt;&#010;&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; Hi Paul,&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; Don't think that I could play with exclusions. Here is an example :&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; *A Unit Test :*&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; *The tested class with ALL traces activated:*&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; *And the same tested class with INFO traces activated:*&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; -----Message d'origine-----&#010;&gt;&gt; De : paulus.benedictus@gmail.com [mailto:paulus.benedictus@gmail.com] De&#010;&gt;&gt; la part de Paul Benedict&#010;&gt;&gt; Envoyé : mercredi 12 février 2014 21:36&#010;&gt;&gt; À : Maven Users List&#010;&gt;&gt; Objet : Re: Code coverage with debug logs: 100% branch coverage not&#010;&gt;&gt; possible?...&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; IIRC, there should be an option in Emma/Cobertura that allows you to&#010;&gt;&gt; exclude coverage on certain classes. So if you can exclude your log4j&#010;&gt;&gt; classes (you don't really want to test your logging, do you?), then you&#010;&gt;&gt; should be able to raise your percentage.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; On Wed, Feb 12, 2014 at 2:30 PM, Benoît Berthonneau&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &lt;benoit@berthonneau.com&gt;wrote:&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; Hi all,&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; I need your opinion/way to tackle the following problem:&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; In many projects we use a Logger (doesn't matter which&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; implementation). It is often recommend to test if the debug level is&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; activated before logging a debug trace like the following:&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; if (logger.isDebugEnabled()) {&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt;     logger.debug("blah " + i + " in the loop that contains " + max);&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; }&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; Now when you run unit tests on this kind of code you need to make a&#010;&gt;&gt; choice:&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; run tests with INFO level or run tests with ALL traces activated. I&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; choose the second option in order to:&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; *         Check that debug traces doesn't throw unwanted exception (like&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; NPE)&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; *         Have a better code coverage in term of covered lines&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; But in term of branches coverage we could never have a 100% :(&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; To me the only way to cover this is to run the tests suite 2 times:&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; one with INFO traces configured, and another one with ALL traces&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; activated.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; Did you face this issue and how did you solve it ?&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; Thanks,&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt; Benoît.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; --&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; Cheers,&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; Paul&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

&#010;&#010;Not really a Maven issue but if you do your logging like this:&#010;&#010;package com.myco.testapp;&#010;import org.slf4j.Logger;&#010;import org.slf4j.LoggerFactory;&#010;&#010;public class MyClass{&#010;             private Logger &#010;_logger=LoggerFactory.getLogger(this.getClass());&#010;&#010;       logger.debug(“blah {} in the loop that contains {}”, i, max);&#010;&#010;}&#010;&#010;You can sort out the enabling of logs and destination of your logging by &#010;severity and class(I think by package as well) in the log configuration &#010;at run-time.&#010;&#010;Ron&#010;&#010;On 12/02/2014 4:20 PM, Mirko Friedenhagen wrote:&#010;&gt; Hello Benoit,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Kevin is right, using slf4j[0] one would use sth. like:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; logger.debug(“blah {} in the loop that contains {}”, i, max);&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; No need for iffing :-).&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; [0] http://www.slf4j.org/manual.html&#010;&gt; Regards Mirko&#010;&gt; --&#010;&gt; http://illegalstateexception.blogspot.com/&#010;&gt; https://github.com/mfriedenhagen/ (http://osrc.dfm.io/mfriedenhagen)&#010;&gt; https://bitbucket.org/mfriedenhagen/&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; On Wed, Feb 12, 2014 at 10:10 PM, Kevin Krumwiede &lt;kjkrum@gmail.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt;&gt; It does matter which implementation. But if&#010;&gt;&gt; you're using a logging API like slf4j that uses parameter replacement&#010;&gt;&gt; tokens in the message string, if the message isn't logged, the replacement&#010;&gt;&gt; won't be performed and the call will be cheap.&#010;&gt;&gt; On Feb 12, 2014 1:57 PM, "Benoît Berthonneau" &lt;benoit@berthonneau.com&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; Hi Paul,&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; Don't think that I could play with exclusions. So if you can exclude your log4j&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; classes (you don't really want to test your logging, do you?), then you&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; should be able to raise your percentage.&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; On Wed, Feb 12, 2014 at 2:30 PM, Benoît Berthonneau&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; &lt;benoit@berthonneau.com&gt;wrote:&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; Hi all,&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; I need your opinion/way to tackle the following problem:&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; In many projects we use a Logger (doesn't matter which&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; implementation). It is often recommend to test if the debug level is&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; activated before logging a debug trace like the following:&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; if (logger.isDebugEnabled()) {&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;     logger.debug("blah " + i + " in the loop that contains " + max);&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; }&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; Now when you run unit tests on this kind of code you need to make a&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; choice:&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; run tests with INFO level or run tests with ALL traces activated. I&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; choose the second option in order to:&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; *         Check that debug traces doesn't throw unwanted exception (like&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; NPE)&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; *         Have a better code coverage in term of covered lines&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; But in term of branches coverage we could never have a 100% :(&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; To me the only way to cover this is to run the tests suite 2 times:&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; one with INFO traces configured, and another one with ALL traces&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; activated.&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; Did you face this issue and how did you solve it ?&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; Thanks,&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; Benoît.&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; --&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; Cheers,&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; Paul&#010;&gt;&gt; ---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;&gt;&gt; To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt;&gt; For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; -- &#010;&gt; Ron Wheeler&#010;&gt; President&#010;&gt; Artifact Software Inc&#010;&gt; email: rwheeler@artifact-software.com&#010;&gt; skype: ronaldmwheeler&#010;&gt; phone: 866-970-2435, ext 102&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; ---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;&gt; To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt; For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt; &#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

My first feeling is that not much time should be spent on that issue,&#010;logging isn't going to take a lot of points of percentage down, having ~95%&#010;would already be great (but maybe you already have).&#010;&#010;Anyway, on the other hand, if what you want is to get code coverage, why&#010;not just enable the ALL logging level when recording code coverage and go&#010;ahead?&#010;&#010;Then, if the verbosity if an issue, simply plug something like an existing&#010;or custom no-op/Null appender [1]? That might sound the simplest solution,&#010;isn't it?&#010;&#010;[1]&#010;https://logging.apache.org/log4j/1.2/apidocs/org/apache/log4j/varia/NullAppender.html&#010;&#010;My 2 cents&#010;&#010;&#010;2014-02-13 7:13 GMT+01:00 Benoît Berthonneau &lt;benoit@berthonneau.com&gt;:&#010;&#010;&gt; Ron, Mirko, Kevin,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Thanks for your feedback : you're right with Slf4j implementation.&#010;&gt; Unfortunately, it is not. The main reason it was&#010;&gt; recommended to&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt; check the logging level was because string concatenation can be&#010;&gt; expensive,&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt; and you want to avoid doing it for a message that won't be logged.&#010;&gt;  But if&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt; you're using a logging API like slf4j that uses parameter replacement&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt; tokens in the message string, if the message isn't logged, the&#010;&gt; replacement&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt; won't be performed and the call will be cheap.&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt; On Feb 12, 2014 1:57 PM, "Benoît Berthonneau" &lt;benoit@berthonneau.com&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; Hi Paul,&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; Don't think that I could play with exclusions. Here is an example :&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; *A Unit Test :*&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; *The tested class with ALL traces activated:*&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; *And the same tested class with INFO traces activated:*&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; -----Message d'origine-----&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; De : paulus.benedictus@gmail.com [mailto:paulus.benedictus@gmail.com]&#010;&gt; De&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; la part de Paul Benedict&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; Envoyé : mercredi 12 février 2014 21:36&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; À : Maven Users List&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; Objet : Re: Code coverage with debug logs: 100% branch coverage not&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; possible?...&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; IIRC, there should be an option in Emma/Cobertura that allows you to&#010;&gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; exclude coverage on certain classes. Re: Code coverage with debug logs: 100% branch coverage not possible?...  
Date  :-
Thu, 13 Feb 2014 09:23:12 GMT  
contents:- 
because if you enable ALL then the other side of the if will not be&#010;followed... you need to combine runs with ALL and NONE to get both sides of&#010;the logging branches.&#010;&#010;Another point that the "slf4j is the solution" camp misses is sometimes the&#010;log message needs evaluation in order to generate the message. For example&#010;you might want to extract a meaningful string representation out of a&#010;complex data structure... with a @CheckFoNull chain of methods to dance&#010;through. While slf4j and other message formatting saves you a lot of the&#010;cases where an `if (debug) { log }` is needed, it does not and can not&#010;eliminate all cases.&#010;&#010;And then there is the final point where you are dealing with a mutable data&#010;structure (this is of more concern with an async logger framework)...&#010;&#010;We had a case whereby the logging statements where logging the object in a&#010;state which it could not possibly be in... because the log formatting and&#010;hence toString() evaluation was taking place in a different thread async&#010;(to prevent logging from slowing down the main code path)... so by the time&#010;the log message was being formatted the object state had mutated and from&#010;&#010;if (!caller.isAuthenticated()) {&#010;  logger.debug("Starting authentication flow for caller {}", caller);&#010;  ...&#010;}&#010;if (StringUtils.isEmpty(caller.getDisplayName) &amp;&amp;&#010;StringUtils.isNotBlank(caller.getCallerId()) {&#010;  logger.debug("Looking up display name of {} using callerId {}", caller,&#010;caller.getCallerId());&#010;  ...&#010;  caller.setDisplayName(displayName);&#010;  logger.debug("Set display name of {} to \"{}\" based on caller id&#010;lookup", caller, displayName);&#010;  ...&#010;}&#010;&#010; you would get&#010;&#010;DEBUG: Starting authentication flow for caller Caller[id=0x67267,&#010;authenticated=true, callerId=+14325551234, displayName="Jim Smith"]&#010;DEBUG: Looking up display name of id=0x67267, authenticated=true,&#010;callerId=+14325551234, displayName="Jim Smith" using callerId +14325551234&#010;DEBUG: Set display name of Caller[id=0x67267, authenticated=true,&#010;callerId=+14325551234, displayName="Jim Smith"] to "Jim Smith" based on&#010;caller id lookup&#010;&#010;which from the code should never happen... what you expect is something like&#010;&#010;DEBUG: Starting authentication flow for caller Caller[id=0x67267,&#010;authenticated=false, callerId=+14325551234, displayName=null]&#010;DEBUG: Looking up display name of Caller[id=0x67267, authenticated=true,&#010;callerId=+14325551234, displayName=null] using callerId +14325551234&#010;DEBUG: Set display name of Caller[id=0x67267, authenticated=true,&#010;callerId=+14325551234, displayName="Jim Smith"] to "Jim Smith" based on&#010;caller id lookup&#010;&#010;But because by the time the DEBUG message was formatted we had mutated the&#010;object state already the logging statements were giving the wrong output...&#010;the fix was to change the code to&#010;&#010;if (!caller.isAuthenticated()) {&#010;  if (logger.isDebug()) logger.debug("Starting authentication flow for&#010;caller {}", caller.toString());&#010;  ...&#010;}&#010;if (StringUtils.isEmpty(caller.getDisplayName) &amp;&amp;&#010;StringUtils.isNotBlank(caller.getCallerId()) {&#010;  if (logger.isDebug()) logger.debug("Looking up display name of {} using&#010;callerId {}", caller.toString(), caller.getCallerId());&#010;  ...&#010;  caller.setDisplayName(displayName);&#010;  if (logger.isDebug()) logger.debug("Set display name of {} to \"{}\"&#010;based on caller id lookup", caller.toString(), displayName);&#010;  ...&#010;}&#010;&#010;In such cases you actually *have to* wrap the logging statement and force&#010;the .toString() when logging.&#010;&#010;What a framework like slf4j and the other message formatting based&#010;frameworks gives you, however, is the default behaviour is lazy toString&#010;and you can add the branches for those cases where you need them.&#010;&#010;-Stephen&#010;&#010;P.S. this logging example is a rephrase of the actual logging code which&#010;using a home baked framework and I have paraphrased the code somewhat,&#010;since this was actually a state machine... but the same issue can occur in&#010;any multi-threaded code base where you are logging mutable objects and&#010;expecting the log formatter to evaluate the toString()&#010;&#010;&#010;On 13 February 2014 08:47, Baptiste Mathus &lt;ml@batmat.net&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; My first feeling is that not much time should be spent on that issue,&#010;&gt; logging isn't going to take a lot of points of percentage down, having ~95%&#010;&gt; would already be great (but maybe you already have).&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Anyway, on the other hand, if what you want is to get code coverage, why&#010;&gt; not just enable the ALL logging level when recording code coverage and go&#010;&gt; ahead?&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Then, if the verbosity if an issue, simply plug something like an existing&#010;&gt; The main reason it was&#010;&gt; &gt; recommended to&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt; check the logging level was because string concatenation can be&#010;&gt; &gt; expensive,&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt; and you want to avoid doing it for a message that won't be logged.&#010;&gt; &gt;  But if&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt; you're using a logging API like slf4j that uses parameter replacement&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt; tokens in the message string, if the message isn't logged, the&#010;&gt; &gt; replacement&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt; won't be performed and the call will be cheap.&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt; On Feb 12, 2014 1:57 PM, "Benoît Berthonneau" &lt;&#010;&gt; benoit@berthonneau.com&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; Hi Paul,&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; Don't think that I could play with exclusions. So if you can exclude your&#010;&gt; log4j&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; classes (you don't really want to test your logging, do you?),&#010;then&#010;&gt; &gt; you&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; should be able to raise your percentage.&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; On Wed, Feb 12, 2014 at 2:30 PM, Benoît Berthonneau&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; &lt;benoit@berthonneau.com&gt;wrote:&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; Hi all,&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; I need your opinion/way to tackle the following problem:&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; In many projects we use a Logger (doesn't matter which&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; implementation). It is often recommend to test if the debug&#010;level&#010;&gt; is&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; activated before logging a debug trace like the following:&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; if (logger.isDebugEnabled()) {&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;     logger.debug("blah " + i + " in the loop that contains&#010;" +&#010;&gt; max);&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; }&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; Now when you run unit tests on this kind of code you need to&#010;make a&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; choice:&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; run tests with INFO level or run tests with ALL traces activated.&#010;I&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; choose the second option in order to:&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; *         Check that debug traces doesn't throw unwanted exception&#010;&gt; &gt; (like&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; NPE)&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; *         Have a better code coverage in term of covered lines&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; But in term of branches coverage we could never have a 100%&#010;:(&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; To me the only way to cover this is to run the tests suite&#010;2 times:&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; one with INFO traces configured, and another one with ALL traces&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; activated.&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; Did you face this issue and how did you solve it ?&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; Thanks,&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; On 13 February 2014 09:23, Stephen Connolly &lt;stephen.alan.connolly@gmail.com&#010;&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; because if you enable ALL then the other side of the if will not be&#010;&gt; followed... you need to combine runs with ALL and NONE to get both sides of&#010;&gt; the logging branches.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Another point that the "slf4j is the solution" camp misses is sometimes&#010;&gt; the log message needs evaluation in order to generate the message. For&#010;&gt; example you might want to extract a meaningful string representation out of&#010;&gt; a complex data structure... with a @CheckFoNull chain of methods to dance&#010;&gt; through. While slf4j and other message formatting saves you a lot of the&#010;&gt; cases where an `if (debug) { log }` is needed, it does not and can not&#010;&gt; eliminate all cases.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; And then there is the final point where you are dealing with a mutable&#010;&gt; data structure (this is of more concern with an async logger framework)...&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; We had a case whereby the logging statements where logging the object in a&#010;&gt; state which it could not possibly be in... because the log formatting and&#010;&gt; hence toString() evaluation was taking place in a different thread async&#010;&gt; (to prevent logging from slowing down the main code path)... so by the time&#010;&gt; the log message was being formatted the object state had mutated and from&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; if (!caller.isAuthenticated()) {&#010;&gt;   logger.debug("Starting authentication flow for caller {}", caller);&#010;&gt;   ...&#010;&gt; }&#010;&gt; if (StringUtils.isEmpty(caller.getDisplayName) &amp;&amp;&#010;&gt; StringUtils.isNotBlank(caller.getCallerId()) {&#010;&gt;   logger.debug("Looking up display name of {} using callerId {}", caller,&#010;&gt; caller.getCallerId());&#010;&gt;   ...&#010;&gt;   caller.setDisplayName(displayName);&#010;&gt;   logger.debug("Set display name of {} to \"{}\" based on caller id&#010;&gt; lookup", caller, displayName);&#010;&gt;   ...&#010;&gt; }&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;  you would get&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; DEBUG: Starting authentication flow for caller Caller[id=0x67267,&#010;&gt; authenticated=true, callerId=+14325551234, displayName="Jim Smith"]&#010;&gt; DEBUG: Looking up display name of id=0x67267, authenticated=true, callerId=&#010;&gt; +14325551234, displayName="Jim Smith" using callerId +14325551234&#010;&gt; DEBUG: Set display name of Caller[id=0x67267, authenticated=true, callerId=&#010;&gt; +14325551234, displayName="Jim Smith"] to "Jim Smith" based on caller id&#010;&gt; lookup&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; which from the code should never happen... what you expect is something&#010;&gt; like&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; DEBUG: Starting authentication flow for caller Caller[id=0x67267,&#010;&gt; authenticated=false, callerId=+14325551234, displayName=null]&#010;&gt; DEBUG: Looking up display name of Caller[id=0x67267, authenticated=true,&#010;&gt; callerId=+14325551234, displayName=null] using callerId +14325551234&#010;&gt; DEBUG: Set display name of Caller[id=0x67267, authenticated=true, callerId=&#010;&gt; +14325551234, displayName="Jim Smith"] to "Jim Smith" based on caller id&#010;&gt; lookup&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; But because by the time the DEBUG message was formatted we had mutated the&#010;&gt; object state already the logging statements were giving the wrong output...&#010;&gt; the fix was to change the code to&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; if (!caller.isAuthenticated()) {&#010;&gt;   if (logger.isDebug()) logger.debug("Starting authentication flow for&#010;&gt; caller {}", caller.toString());&#010;&gt;   ...&#010;&gt; }&#010;&gt; if (StringUtils.isEmpty(caller.getDisplayName) &amp;&amp;&#010;&gt; StringUtils.isNotBlank(caller.getCallerId()) {&#010;&gt;   if (logger.isDebug()) logger.debug("Looking up display name of {} using&#010;&gt; callerId {}", caller.toString(), caller.getCallerId());&#010;&gt;   ...&#010;&gt;   caller.setDisplayName(displayName);&#010;&gt;   if (logger.isDebug()) logger.debug("Set display name of {} to \"{}\"&#010;&gt; based on caller id lookup", caller.toString(), displayName);&#010;&gt;   ...&#010;&gt; }&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; In such cases you actually *have to* wrap the logging statement and force&#010;&gt; the .toString() when logging&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;Well there are other solutions such as switching to immutable objects...&#010;but if you don't have the ability to make such a change...&#010;&#010;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; What a framework like slf4j and the other message formatting based&#010;&gt; frameworks gives you, however, is the default behaviour is lazy toString&#010;&gt; and you can add the branches for those cases where you need them.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; -Stephen&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; P.S. this logging example is a rephrase of the actual logging code which&#010;&gt; using a home baked framework and I have paraphrased the code somewhat,&#010;&gt; since this was actually a state machine... but the same issue can occur in&#010;&gt; any multi-threaded code base where you are logging mutable objects and&#010;&gt; expecting the log formatter to evaluate the toString()&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; On 13 February 2014 08:47, Baptiste Mathus &lt;ml@batmat.net&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; My first feeling is that not much time should be spent on that issue,&#010;&gt;&gt; logging isn't going to take a lot of points of percentage down, having&#010;&gt;&gt; ~95%&#010;&gt;&gt; would already be great (but maybe you already have).&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; Anyway, on the other hand, if what you want is to get code coverage, why&#010;&gt;&gt; not just enable the ALL logging level when recording code coverage and go&#010;&gt;&gt; Re: Code coverage with debug logs: 100% branch coverage not possible?...  
Date  :-
Thu, 13 Feb 2014 16:28:24 GMT  
contents:- 
 &#010;&#010;Thanks for all your comments. I will conclude to my first idea: tests&#010;need to be run 2 times (one with traces to OFF or INFO, and the other&#010;one with traces to ALL) &#010;&#010;Regards, &#010;&#010;Benoît. &#010;&#010;Le 13-02-2014 10:25, Stephen Connolly a écrit : &#010;&#010;&gt; On 13 February 2014 09:23, Stephen Connolly &lt;stephen.alan.connolly@gmail.com&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt; because if you enable ALL then the other side of the if will not be followed... you&#010;need to combine runs with ALL and NONE to get both sides of the logging branches. Another&#010;point that the "slf4j is the solution" camp misses is sometimes the log message needs evaluation&#010;in order to generate the message. For example you might want to extract a meaningful string&#010;representation out of a complex data structure... with a @CheckFoNull chain of methods to&#010;dance through. While slf4j and other message formatting saves you a lot of the cases where&#010;an `if (debug) { log }` is needed, it does not and can not eliminate all cases. And then there&#010;is the final point where you are dealing with a mutable data structure (this is of more concern&#010;with an async logger framework)... We had a case whereby the logging statements where logging&#010;the object in a state which it could not possibly be in... because the log formatting and&#010;hence toString() evaluation was taking place in a different thread async (to&#010;prevent logging from slowing down the main code path)... so by the time the log message was&#010;being formatted the object state had mutated and from if (!caller.isAuthenticated()) { logger.debug("Starting&#010;authentication flow for caller {}", caller); ... } if (StringUtils.isEmpty(caller.getDisplayName)&#010;&amp;&amp; StringUtils.isNotBlank(caller.getCallerId()) { logger.debug("Looking up display&#010;name of {} using callerId {}", caller, caller.getCallerId()); ... caller.setDisplayName(displayName);&#010;logger.debug("Set display name of {} to "{}" based on caller id lookup", caller, displayName);&#010;... } you would get DEBUG: Starting authentication flow for caller Caller[id=0x67267, authenticated=true,&#010;callerId=+14325551234, displayName="Jim Smith"] DEBUG: Looking up display name of id=0x67267,&#010;authenticated=true, callerId= +14325551234, displayName="Jim Smith" using callerId +14325551234&#010;DEBUG: Set display name of Caller[id=0x67267, authenticated=true, callerId= +14325551234,&#010;displayName="Jim Smith"] to "Jim&#010;Smith" based on caller id lookup which from the code should never happen... what you expect&#010;is something like DEBUG: Starting authentication flow for caller Caller[id=0x67267, authenticated=false,&#010;callerId=+14325551234, displayName=null] DEBUG: Looking up display name of Caller[id=0x67267,&#010;authenticated=true, callerId=+14325551234, displayName=null] using callerId +14325551234 DEBUG:&#010;Set display name of Caller[id=0x67267, authenticated=true, callerId= +14325551234, displayName="Jim&#010;Smith"] to "Jim Smith" based on caller id lookup But because by the time the DEBUG message&#010;was formatted we had mutated the object state already the logging statements were giving the&#010;wrong output... the fix was to change the code to if (!caller.isAuthenticated()) { if (logger.isDebug())&#010;logger.debug("Starting authentication flow for caller {}", caller.toString()); ... } if (StringUtils.isEmpty(caller.getDisplayName)&#010;&amp;&amp; StringUtils.isNotBlank(caller.getCallerId()) { if (logger.isDebug())&#010;logger.debug("Looking up display name of {} using callerId {}", caller.toString(), caller.getCallerId());&#010;... caller.setDisplayName(displayName); if (logger.isDebug()) logger.debug("Set display name&#010;of {} to "{}" based on caller id lookup", caller.toString(), displayName); ... } In such cases&#010;you actually *have to* wrap the logging statement and force the .toString() when logging&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; Well there are other solutions such as switching to immutable objects...&#010;&gt; but if you don't have the ability to make such a change...&#010;&gt; What a framework like slf4j and the other message formatting based frameworks gives you,&#010;however, is the default behaviour is lazy toString and you can add the branches for those&#010;cases where you need them. -Stephen P.S. this logging example is a rephrase of the actual&#010;logging code which using a home baked framework and I have paraphrased the code somewhat,&#010;since this was actually a state machine... but the same issue can occur in any multi-threaded&#010;code base where you are logging mutable objects and expecting the log formatter to evaluate&#010;the toString() On 13 February 2014 08:47, Baptiste Mathus &lt;ml@batmat.net&gt; wrote: My&#010;first feeling is that not much time should be spent on that issue, logging isn't going to&#010;take a lot of points of percentage down, having ~95% would already be great (but maybe you&#010;already have). Anyway, on the other hand, if what you want is to get code coverage, why not&#010;just enable the ALL logging level when recording code coverage and go ahead? Then, if the&#010;verbosity if an issue, simply plug something like an existing or custom no-op/Null appender&#010;[1]? That might sound the simplest solution, isn't it? [1] https://logging.apache.org/log4j/1.2/apidocs/org/apache/log4j/varia/NullAppender.html&#010;[1] My 2 cents 2014-02-13 7:13 GMT+01:00 Benoît Berthonneau &lt;benoit@berthonneau.com&gt;:&#010;Ron, Mirko, Kevin, Thanks for your feedback : you're right with Slf4j implementation. Unfortunately,&#010;it is not. It is a home made logger interface implemented by Log4j. Benoît Le 12 févr. 2014&#010;à 23:25, Ron Wheeler &lt;rwheeler@artifact-software.com a écrit : Not really a Maven issue&#010;but if you do your logging like this: package com.myco.testapp; import org.slf4j.Logger; import&#010;org.slf4j.LoggerFactory; public class MyClass{ private Logger _logger=LoggerFactory.getLogger(this.getClass());&#010;logger.debug("blah {} in the loop that contains {}", i, max); } You can sort out the enabling&#010;of logs and destination of your logging&#010; by &#010;&#010;&gt; severity and class(I think by package as well) in the log configuration&#010; at &#010;&#010;&gt; run-time. [0] http://www.slf4j.org/manual.html [2] Regards Mirko&#010;-- http://illegalstateexception.blogspot.com/ [3] https://github.com/mfriedenhagen/ [4] (http://osrc.dfm.io/mfriedenhagen&#010;[5]) https://bitbucket.org/mfriedenhagen/ [6] On Wed, Feb 12, 2014 at 10:10 PM, Kevin Krumwiede&#010;&lt;kjkrum@gmail.com&#010; wrote: &#010;&#010;&gt; It does matter which implementation. The main reason it was&#010; recommended to &#010;&#010;&gt; check the logging level was because string concatenation can be&#010; expensive, &#010;&#010;&gt; and you want to avoid doing it for a message that won't be logged.&#010; But if &#010;&#010;&gt; you're using a logging API like slf4j that uses parameter&#010; replacement &#010;&#010;&gt; tokens in the message string, if the message isn't logged, the&#010; replacement &#010;&#010;&gt; won't be performed and the call will be cheap. On Feb 12, 2014 1:57 PM, "Benoît Berthonneau"&#010;&lt;&#010; benoit@berthonneau.com&gt; &#010;&#010;&gt; wrote: Hi Paul, Don't think that I could play with exclusions. It is often&#010;recommend to test if the debug level&#010; is &#010;&#010;&gt; activated before logging a debug trace like the following: if (logger.isDebugEnabled())&#010;{ logger.debug("blah " + i + " in the loop that contains " +&#010; max); &#010;&#010;&gt; } Now when you run unit tests on this kind of code you need to make&#010; a &#010;&#010;&gt; choice: run tests with INFO level or run tests with ALL traces activated.&#010; I &#010;&#010;&gt; choose the second option in order to: * Check that debug traces doesn't throw unwanted&#010;exception&#010; (like &#010;&#010;&gt; NPE) * Have a better code coverage in term of covered lines But in term of branches coverage&#010;we could never have a 100% :( To me the only way to cover this is to run the tests suite 2&#010; times: &#010;&#010;&gt; one with INFO traces configured, and another one with ALL traces activated. Did you face&#010;this issue and how did you solve it ? Re: Code coverage with debug logs: 100% branch coverage not possible?...  
Date  :-
Fri, 14 Feb 2014 12:54:37 GMT  
contents:- 
I have also been annoyed with what you describe, and have wondered how&#010;to fill the gap of missing coverage.&#010;&#010;Outside of copying the testcase and dynamically changing the log level&#010;inside of it, which in addition to being burdensome, also offends my&#010;DRY sensibility, the best idea I've had about this involves a&#010;relatively new feature of JUnit called @Theories[1].&#010;&#010;You could create @DataPoints {Level.ALL, Level.NONE} and then pass&#010;them in to your test method. Then you dynamically set the class under&#010;test's Logger.Level with the data point. I think this ought to work&#010;just fine unless you execute your tests in parallel mode, as most&#010;Logger declarations are as static instances.&#010;&#010;There's one other problem which has prevented me from exploiting this&#010;technique: @Theories needs a dedicated @RunWith(Theories.class). Which&#010;would tend to preclude execution under @RunWith(Arquillian.class)&#010;since @RunWith takes a singular runner argument, unless Aslak/someone&#010;makes some tweaks[2].&#010;&#010;[1] https://github.com/junit-team/junit/wiki/Theories&#010;[2] https://issues.jboss.org/browse/ARQ-561&#010;&#010;&#010;On Wed, Feb 12, 2014 at 3:30 PM, Benoît Berthonneau&#010;&lt;benoit@berthonneau.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt; Hi all,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I need your opinion/way to tackle the following problem:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; In many projects we use a Logger (doesn't matter which implementation). It&#010;&gt; is often recommend to test if the debug level is activated before logging a&#010;&gt; debug trace like the following:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; if (logger.isDebugEnabled()) {&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;     logger.debug("blah " + i + " in the loop that contains " + max);&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; }&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Now when you run unit tests on this kind of code you need to make a choice:&#010;&gt; run tests with INFO level or run tests with ALL traces activated. I choose&#010;&gt; the second option in order to:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; *         Check that debug traces doesn't throw unwanted exception (like&#010;&gt; NPE)&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; *         Have a better code coverage in term of covered lines&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; But in term of branches coverage we could never have a 100% :(&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; To me the only way to cover this is to run the tests suite 2 times: one with&#010;&gt; INFO traces configured, and another one with ALL traces activated.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Did you face this issue and how did you solve it ?&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Thanks,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Benoît.&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

contents:- 
You should really restart with the module 2 pom.&#010;&#010;Your multi-module structure is good. You have a separate projekt/module&#010;which creates your distro. What you should do is to create the "distro"&#010;(zip or whatever) to be created as part of the normal build and then&#010;deployed as the project's artifact it is.&#010;This is done in many projects and you could for example have a look at the&#010;Maven core project where we create a zip and a tar file.&#010;https://git-wip-us.apache.org/repos/asf?p=maven.git;a=tree;f=apache-maven;hb=HEAD&#010;&#010;So in the end, you will not use deploy:deploy-file. Also, your pom will be&#010;very small with pretty much only the m-assembly-p being bound to the build&#010;lifecycle.&#010;&#010;/Anders&#010;&#010;&#010;On Thu, Feb 13, 2014 at 11:36 AM, Henrik Skriver Rasmussen &lt;&#010;skriver79@gmail.com&gt; Hi Henrik,&#010;&#010;IMHO deploy-file (just like install-file) should *never* be a part of a  &#010;lifecycle, but should be run standalone and should only be used for  &#010;unavailable third party artifacts.&#010;&#010;Looking back at your pom-fragment, you should do the following:&#010;* if "deploymentfile" is being created by a Maven plugin, try to make that  &#010;plugin attach that file to the project.&#010;* Use  &#010;http://mojo.codehaus.org/build-helper-maven-plugin/attach-artifact-mojo.html  &#010;and remove the deploy-file asap. This plugin does it's work as part of the  &#010;build lifecycle as it should be.&#010;&#010;Robert&#010;&#010;Op Sun, 16 Feb 2014 11:20:39 +0100 schreef Henrik Skriver Rasmussen  &#010;&lt;skriver79@gmail.com&gt;:&#010;&#010;&gt; Hi Robert&#010;&gt; Thank you for your answer.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I would like to figure out how to simple skip the generation of the given&#010;&gt; extra zip file because I do not know how now.&#010;&gt; Any way to see during debug which goal will result in which artifact? Any&#010;&gt; help on finding out when running my build will be appreciated.&#010;&gt; I can not omit what I do not know to control nor can I not attach it  &#010;&gt; when I&#010;&gt; do no what generates it.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Not creating or attaching the artifact solves the problem - but still, as&#010;&gt; user of maven I still say that it is counter intuitive to have the&#010;&gt; deploy-file goal not only deploy the specified file.&#010;&gt; The deploy goal should deploy all - but not the deploy-file goal. :)&#010;&gt; I know that is a different discussion about meaningful naming of APIs and&#010;&gt; frankly I don't care now that I know.&#010;&gt; But maven developers should care about simplifying and make maven APIs&#010;&gt; intuitive since maven is not exactly gaining ground due to it's  &#010;&gt; simplicity&#010;&gt; and transparency. ;)&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; That being said, I have been using maven for a looong time and enjoy it&#010;&gt; most of the time - so keep up the good work!&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; regards&#010;&gt; Henrik Skriver Rasmussen&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; On Sun, Feb 16, 2014 at 2:03 PM, Robert Scholte  &#010;&gt; &lt;rfscholte@apache.org&gt;wrote:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; Op Sun, 16 Feb 2014 08:15:25 +0100 schreef Henrik Skriver Rasmussen &lt;&#010;&gt;&gt; skriver79@gmail.com&gt;:&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;  Thanks for the advice on how to restructure.&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; Could you have a look at the deploy-plugin project and the file&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; org.apache.maven.plugin.deploy.DeployFileMojo execute method line 376  &#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; in&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; version 2.8.1 ? I would really like to understand the following:&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; 1) What controls which artifacts are attached the model for the given&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; project?&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; The plugin creating that artifact controls the attaching. For example:&#010;&gt;&gt; http://maven.apache.org/plugins/maven-source-plugin/&#010;&gt;&gt; xref/org/apache/maven/plugin/source/AbstractSourceJarMojo.html#307&#010;&gt;&gt; Here the -sources.jar is attached to the project.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;  2) Is it possible to state that no artifacts except explicitly stated&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; should be created/attached?&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; The plugin creating that artifact&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;  3) Is it really the intended behaviour of the deploy:file goal to also&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; deploy the attached artifacts? To me that is a very non-intuitive&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; behaviour.&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; Yes. If there are attachments created and these are attached, they are&#010;&gt;&gt; uploaded as well. So if you don't want this, solve it at the source, i.e&#010;&gt;&gt; the plugin creating the artifact. (for the maven-source-plugin: skip it&#010;&gt;&gt; (best option) or just don't attach (acceptable option) )&#010;&gt;&gt; For the same reason you won't find "delete" options in any of the  &#010;&gt;&gt; plugins.&#010;&gt;&gt; It is a matter of excluding the correct files.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; Robert&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; I Basically have a working setup which deploys the zip file I generate  &#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; to&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; repo with the name I have specified. But the only thing that bothers  &#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; me is&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; that for some unclear reason the same zip is deployed again with the  &#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; name&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; of the project in the same deploy:file goal. Jörg Schaible &lt;joerg.schai...@swisspost.com&gt;  
Subject  :-
Re: How to minimize quantity of profiles in pom.xml file  
Date  :-
Fri, 14 Feb 2014 11:49:43 GMT  
contents:- 
fred wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; I need to build project for many kinds of environment so i need a lot of&#010;&gt; profiles with settings for this env.&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; There is a cutted module pom.xml -  pom.xml file&#010;&gt; &lt;http://www.mediafire.com/view/47gt5jiegta7auq/pom.xml&gt;&#010;&#010;All you need in the profile is a simple property:&#010;&#010;===================== %&lt; ====================&#010; &lt;build&gt;&#010;   &lt;plugins&gt;&#010;     ...&#010;     &lt;plugin&gt;&#010;       ... your plugin ...&#010;       &lt;configuration&gt;&#010;        ... your configuration ...&#010;        &lt;targetURL&gt;http://${profile.host}:&#010;${port}/crx/packmgr/service.jsp&lt;/targetURL&gt;&#010;       &lt;/configuration&gt;&#010;       ...&#010;     &lt;/plugin&gt;&#010;   &lt;/plugins&gt;&#010;   ...&#010; &lt;/build&gt;&#010; &lt;profiles&gt;&#010;   &lt;profile&gt;&#010;     &lt;id&gt;auto-deploy&lt;/id&gt;&#010;     &lt;properties&gt;&#010;       &lt;profile.host&gt;${host}&lt;/profile.host&gt;&#010;     &lt;/properties&gt;&#010;   &lt;/profile&gt;&#010;   &lt;profile&gt;&#010;     &lt;id&gt;dev&lt;/id&gt;&#010;     &lt;properties&gt;&#010;       &lt;profile.host&gt;${dev.host}&lt;/profile.host&gt;&#010;     &lt;/properties&gt;&#010;   &lt;/profile&gt;&#010;   ...&#010; &lt;/profiles&gt;&#010;===================== %&lt; ====================&#010;&#010;As rule of thumb: Just put the stuff into the profile that *is* actually &#010;different.&#010;&#010;- Jörg&#010;&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

But now i must execute a maven plugin, that should be executed after&#010;the submodule build was finished. Is this possible, and when not, how can i&#010;realize this? The parent pom is only a aggregator pom.&#010;&#010;Thank you in Advance!&#010;&#010;Regards,&#010;Denis&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;--&#010;View this message in context: http://maven.40175.n5.nabble.com/Maven-parent-POM-execute-plugin-after-the-submodule-execution-tp5784481.html&#010;Sent from the Maven - Users mailing list archive at Nabble.com.&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Name  :- 
Wayne Fay &lt;wayne...@gmail.com&gt;  
Subject  :-
Re: Maven parent POM - execute plugin after the submodule execution  
Date  :-
Fri, 14 Feb 2014 06:46:38 GMT  
contents:- 
Just add another submodule.&#010;Make it depend on the "last" submodule (eg you had A, B, C before -&#010;make this D, and depend on C, assumes C depends on B which depends on&#010;A).&#010;Add the plugin to D.&#010;&#010;Wayne&#010;&#010;On Thu, Feb 13, 2014 at 7:04 AM, DenisDasKind &lt;bltomov@abv.bg&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt; Hi Everybody, in my project i have a pom, that contains some childs&#010;&gt; (submodules). The parent pom is only a aggregator pom.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Thank you in Advance!&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Regards,&#010;&gt; Denis&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; --&#010;&gt; View this message in context: http://maven.40175.n5.nabble.com/Maven-parent-POM-execute-plugin-after-the-submodule-execution-tp5784481.html&#010;&gt; Sent from the Maven - Users mailing list archive at Nabble.com.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; ---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;&gt; To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt; For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Date  :-
Thu, 13 Feb 2014 17:50:46 GMT  
contents:- 
I'll make it short: please don't use reportPlugins in m-site-p configuration&#010;&#010;see http://maven.apache.org/plugins/maven-site-plugin/maven-3.html#Configuration_formats&#010;&#010;use classic configuration and everything will work fine&#010;&#010;Regards,&#010;&#010;Hervé&#010;&#010;Le jeudi 13 février 2014 15:34:03 Alex Potsides a écrit :&#010;&gt; I'm sorry if this question has been asked already but I couldn't find much&#010;&gt; in the archives.&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; I'm trying to convert some existing build plugins to instead be report&#010;&gt; plugins with v3.3 of maven-site-plugin.  One of the plugins needs an extra&#010;&gt; dependency to be specified.  When it lived as a direct child of&#010;&gt; build/plugins this was ok, but when I do this sort of thing:&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &lt;plugin&gt;&#010;&gt;   &lt;artifactId&gt;maven-site-plugin&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;&gt;   &lt;version&gt;3.3&lt;/version&gt;&#010;&gt;   &lt;configuration&gt;&#010;&gt;     &lt;reportPlugins&gt;&#010;&gt;      &lt;plugin&gt;&#010;&gt;        &lt;groupId&gt;..&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;&gt;        &lt;artifactId&gt;..&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;&gt;        &lt;version&gt;..&lt;/version&gt;&#010;&gt;        &lt;dependencies&gt;&#010;&gt;          &lt;dependency&gt;&#010;&gt;            &lt;artifactId&gt;..&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;&gt;            &lt;groupId&gt;..&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;&gt;            ...&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; I get:&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; Cannot find setter, adder nor field in&#010;&gt; org.apache.maven.reporting.exec.ReportPlugin for 'dependencies'&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; Is this sort of configuration not possible?&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; Thanks in advance.&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; Alex Potsides&#010;&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Name  :- 
DenisDasKind &lt;blto...@abv.bg&gt;  
Subject  :-
Re: Prevent installing archives to local repository  
Date  :-
Mon, 17 Feb 2014 08:42:48 GMT  
contents:- 
I have take a look, and found that each file, created with the maven assembly&#010;plugin was installed to the local repository under the project name. In my&#010;case the maven assembly plugin creates a file abc.zip that is part of the&#010;distribution, and maven install plugin installed the abs.zip to the local&#010;repository as projectName.zip and the distribution file.&#010;My idea is to skip the installation of abc.zip to the repository because it&#010;is only temporary needed, and is part of the distribution zip file.&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;--&#010;View this message in context: http://maven.40175.n5.nabble.com/Prevent-installing-archives-to-local-repository-tp5784848p5785132.html&#010;Sent from the Maven - Users mailing list archive at Nabble.com.&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Name  :- 
Karl Heinz Marbaise &lt;khmarba...@gmx.de&gt;  
Subject  :-
Re: Prevent installing archives to local repository  
Date  :-
Mon, 17 Feb 2014 08:54:03 GMT  
contents:- 
Hi,&#010;&#010; &gt; I have take a look, and found that each file, created with the maven &#010;assembly&#010;&gt; plugin was installed to the local repository under the project name. In my&#010;&gt; case the maven assembly plugin creates a file abc.zip that is part of the&#010;&gt; distribution, and maven install plugin installed the abs.zip to the local&#010;&gt; repository as projectName.zip and the distribution file.&#010;&gt; My idea is to skip the installation of abc.zip to the repository because it&#010;&gt; is only temporary needed, and is part of the distribution zip file.&#010;&#010;There is an parameter for the maven-assembly-plugin&#010;http://maven.apache.org/plugins/maven-assembly-plugin/single-mojo.html&#010;&#010;which allows to suppress attaching an artifact in particular if you have &#010;intermediate results which you don't like to attach to the project..&#010;&#010;&lt;attach&gt;false&lt;/attach&gt;&#010;&#010;which needs having a separate execution block...&#010;&#010;Kind regards&#010;Karl-Heinz Marbaise&#010;&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

&gt; I've written a Windows batch file to invoke Maven to build the project&#010;&gt; before I choose Jenkins as my daily build system. And at that time I got&#010;&gt; the same Maven error as I described in this thread.&#010;&#010;Maven calls out to your system JDK to do the compilation step. With&#010;the [ERROR] lines you provided previously, Maven is simply passing&#010;along the error that was reported by javac. I bet, if you constructed&#010;the proper javac call (which can be seen in Maven's logs if you use -X&#010;for debug mode), you would see the same error produced without&#010;involving Maven (or Jenkins) at all.&#010;&#010;IIRC you had some "cannot find symbol" errors. What do you expect&#010;Maven to do about code defects reported by the Java compiler? Why are&#010;you blaming Maven for this?&#010;&#010;&gt; I'll post some other source code and POM files later. Please help me to&#010;&gt; diagnose my problem then. Thanks.&#010;&#010;Please don't try to send attachments or huge logs, source code, pom&#010;files to the list. Is it possible that you have more than 1 version of Java installed?&#010;I use Eclipse/STS,  have all the Maven tools that I need to build with &#010;Maven so I may suggest some things that you may not have, with m2 &#010;installed separately.&#010;&#010;1) Look in the project properties and make sure that you have nothing &#010;specified as a library besides Maven dependencies. (libraries might be &#010;configured in Eclipse that you are not setting in other builds)&#010;2) Make sure that you do not allow Eclipse to use other project &#010;workspaces for resolution of dependencies.(Eclipse will look in other &#010;eclipse projects to find dependencies).&#010;3) Make sure that you are using the "right" java compiler from Eclipse. &#010;It is easy to get different compilers in play.&#010;&#010;&#010;If you do all this, you may find that your Eclipse build fails in the &#010;same way that your other builds fail.&#010;You can then fix them both up to be the same.&#010;&#010;I hope that this helps.&#010;&#010;Ron&#010;&#010;n 16/02/2014 10:15 AM, LevskiWeng wrote:&#010;&gt; Thanks for your suggestion. But I don't think it's the Jenkins fault&#010;&gt; because:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I've written a Windows batch file to invoke Maven to build the project&#010;&gt; before I choose Jenkins as my daily build system. And at that time I got&#010;&gt; the same Maven error as I described in this thread.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I'll post some other source code and POM files later. Please help me to&#010;&gt; diagnose my problem then. Thanks.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; P.S:&#010;&gt; I'll diagnose my POM configuration of package dependency, and I'll post the&#010;&gt; result here tomorrow.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; On Sun, Feb 16, 2014 at 2:59 AM, stephenconnolly [via Maven] &lt;&#010;&gt; ml-node+s40175n5785002h44@n5.nabble.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; http://javaadventure.blogspot.ie/2013/11/jenkins-maven-job-type-considered-evil.html&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; Using the evil one makes Maven behave in ways that it doesn't intend to...&#010;&gt;&gt; Please try with a FreeStyle job using a Maven Build step to see if it is&#010;&gt;&gt; the evil job type causing issues for you&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; --&#010;&gt; Levski Weng&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; --&#010;&gt; View this message in context: http://maven.40175.n5.nabble.com/Why-does-Maven-fail-to-compile-my-project-occasionally-tp5784849p5785057.html&#010;&gt; Sent from the Maven - Users mailing list archive at Nabble.com.&#010;&#010;&#010;-- &#010;Ron Wheeler&#010;President&#010;Artifact Software Inc&#010;email: rwheeler@artifact-software.com&#010;skype: ronaldmwheeler&#010;phone: 866-970-2435, ext 102&#010;&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Robert Scholte-4 wrote&#010;&gt; "My code is correct because I could successfully build the whole project  &#010;&gt; in Eclipse again and again."&#010;&gt; This is 100% true. Within Eclipse you can manually add libraries.  &#010;&gt; Actually, if you create your first JUnit test, Eclipse will ask if the  &#010;&gt; JUnit4 library should be added. If you do so, it's added as an Eclipse  &#010;&gt; library, but your Maven build won't have junit as a dependency, resulting  &#010;&gt; in uncompilable tests.&#010;&#010;I'm add all necessary dependent libraries that I know in pom.xml. It looks&#010;weird and I've no idea about it. Could you help me to diagnose the problem&#010;further?&#010;&#010;&#010;Robert Scholte-4 wrote&#010;&gt; Did you open this file?&#010;&gt; AgentIdResourceMapIpHandle.java:[36,24] refers to line 36, column 24. Just  &#010;&gt; open that file with notepad (copy/paste the fully qualified path to ensure  &#010;&gt; you're picking up the correct file, not some copy)&#010;&gt; Where is that "symbol"/Class coming from?
